Forbes' Homepage Pitch


The corporate and wealth news magazine's latest homepage revamping is focused, in part, on raising the profile of marketers in its AdVoice program, which integrates advertiser posts with user and staff content. As Lewis DVorkin, Forbes Media's chief product officer writes in a blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015VMijExHsyR2PPN4xa3EOlLnNxIt011aYdjpDpadNLikKC6lqa1ROggM3UebCsYNkePHDIh7z5FTrB536mIB4rVCRQyMVkcEL4QYki3T-f9pbf1jyjuKC6ITJA9IYapR9jfMcqDmm3FqUKMPi71xn1swRffqtUNaVsn1uGbgb4AwlJGoQhIiDf_6AO21hCdyo4ZOE8zTBq1BA9SBgjiW2zG9cZwAogavr7-0wwjSTm_8ow0cxAH0FQ==> , marketers are content producers too, right? So they now have a cleaner canvas to "publish -- not pitch," says DVorkin, and reach consumers amenable to a message that mixes both. 


Valuing Personal Data


Angel investor Jerry Neumann's latest blog post title says it all from his perspective: "Your personal data is not worth anywhere near what you think it's worth." He reviews his Root Markets business days and concludes, "I spent several years of my life trying to build a business that lets people take control of their own data while still leaving a way for marketers to find them. I believe in privacy. And I believe that marketers finding customers is key to economic efficiency. I would love to see someone square this circle, but the Root model is not the way to do it." Read what he means. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015VMijExHsyTK8yriscf31YI4veG4IL36pUHmyF-WYh9npAUHoJEoWtvl-qQs_048WB1shiUqdx6q9c9WJTX6JV5fJ-kfrr9IzOfx4tIsvQk1a3Z4ks8PNen2x4NkQplQnT7Bdy9EfQr0jNg1MGOs-XxEhxB4KhYFXvGune7ymXzNjCGx_NhHY02BKuTBsIXp>  


The EU Cookie Compliance


The wave of European Union regulation over how publishers and employ user data in the ha nevertheless allowed sites a great degree of discretion in how they let individuals opt out of being targeted. Either that, or as Econsultancy's David Moth explains, the regulators don't have a clue about how to inform consumers. To give readers a clue about how the policy is being adopted, EConsultancy has helpfully posted some 20-odd examples of how publishers are muddling through. Scroll through here. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015VMijExHsyT9q0H-NSbmX2tHSnprEWDxAYCisSJmLnRwUZvPxKTMHEqMZwejRMBuYfxV1G0213xesBKZBSyLWpWZrwGi98TCVXGeX0NVxoZS_130Ncor90Mvy6UO2JkfYRjkUK--v3xzoWg0BaAlVtOnvbpJkwsDBKgW01DyzJGT_hxEyo-F-HHfMPKnDPyC>  


Tagging And Attributing


Tag manager BrightTag announced new biz dev partnerships yesterday as it looks to analytics consultancies to help leverage the data capture enabled through the BrightTag One platform. Companies include Blast Advanced Media, Cardinal Path, The Encima Group, Keystone Solutions, Semphonic and WebHue. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015VMijExHsyQD2q5HYoYoDLjjCYlA1wB2M4EMNh0e9meM6vA_3UUbib992SbnAqnU0Xq7dYOQSpHXBvRh8WFoceumB8zNHW5YZtwi5EmnZgyMssRrU56y4bwjOjMJzflM_oo-csJeDh8ICFYfSyjEmDH4T5O--iNovuUUXDOjYfX0qkWL5ku-FDMHdv6Hql7y_G9Juzj4UNngKhWW7865owkpH3vRFsis0APyXkWliEAUnnYEBdJ08A-f_VLVavHqfFr0PhX_wX0=>  Likewise, Adometry has reached out to media agency Empower to push out its toolkit. The release states, "Under the terms of the agreement, Empower will offer the Adometry ad analytics suite to clients as part of the agency's Decision Sciences service, including LasikPlus Vision Centers, Marzetti and U.S. Bank." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015VMijExHsySMsZNIpuEAHpS0RpuTPGbhKY_jYO-Zhz70f7mrH0kMBfust1EjlvSoul0XcDbzZIMJtLFVZFgtbNYMvbneZ7vq9d__bTN8sxBSDGRWx8wosABxlK5oe7RCxxEX9DQ3bwB735i9vBD_-w==>  


Counting The Spend


Q1 2012 showed a continued increase in global ad spend according to Nielsen. Looking cross-borders: "Emerging markets like the Middle East and Africa saw double-digit increases while North America and Asia Pacific saw modest more gains of 2.1 and 1.7 percent, respectively. Overall global ad spend in Q1 2012 was $128 billion USD." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015VMijExHsyQbaEQl6X5qQsY8qvtngemHoPBOGkmth6ftdzni0gSigiCh-gDbjZv1t-wZpcZ-_T3RyQCVhvuF1t07S9j2NZWrwTMVs_Eyj-9yjZZam3ZNeZNswx7aYjv-K9-maT7WKna3RrLvKOiuA_5ybYhZuudf7CkKbCTfIPbcgUMtwtIrdXr45r_qVmfS5B67OR_ZQLLtypeTGemjwcqao0ioN9gx0h4qrO4dgrLEBy0_kNkJbA==>

Rocket Funds


All Things D's Peter Kafka brings news of the latest ad tech fundraising event as Rocket Fuel has captured $50 million (that's $76 mil total). Kafka writes, "Rocket Fuel says it generated gross revenue of $45 million last year, but bear in mind that the company's net revenue, after factoring in the cost of the ad inventory it buys for its clients, will be much less than that. Still, John says that in the last couple months his company has hit a $100 million annual run rate, so he has a growth story to tell." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015VMijExHsyRF2ZP7FhpNKQLA1USWuSV8iXpHvTBqO-BGP2cMYMojNZdjUVuAmQ5KXNYFLPTjJEmUgJOcrrSul8nHrji9tlJdcb7u19lkEMVkHrPVsCURbwIYMasJeVRa2Z0rA7rAIv1dYpsIBT5WhV52QcLP8jv-SoAfl7Ij_-tI1T46EsB2TMDx9DBNx-2WFinn1PFa-t4=>  And, read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015VMijExHsyRSM3_GcoDljCGiTrWF9OYzJUFJ88SGcTeWXdxkZS8hyxWJwyjOvUukPuBEYyiFZrOeUwuwLGly7OcofHk-zkYFhsQAHs29H1aRG9M6Wk6RWpdrrPU3aTBwX-3F6KRKcVWCZ2ebeI5S5YdzXiweHRymxYu1oZI5TdS6xnHTr9F-1Qr2wG0QSMMxJ1TCLcAqbqfLxLjuzBgeRDhVjlNVke9UgyuE0RYfMTBpk-Btje-bVQ==>  


Mobilizing The SSP


In a continuing effort to execute on the mobile front, sell-side platform PubMatic has hired former Ringleader Digital CEO Bob Walczak. The release says that in addition to his CEO experience, "at Ringleader, Walczak was responsible for all business development and closed pioneering contracts with AOL, Microsoft, AccuWeather, Fox News, ESPN and Collective Media." Studying Facebook Ads


A new survey on Facebook ad efficicacy leaves the reader wondering - just wondering - because there are so many opinions on whether the ads work or not Ad Age's Michael Learmonth introduces the results of the study crafted by his publication and Citigroup: "When it comes to Facebook, the nation's marketers have reached an overwhelming consensus: you simply have to be there. Unfortunately for Facebook, they also have reached another: advertising on Facebook isn't necessarily required." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZENM8bLBvkby0vhExYqSJYN9pUXvqjTKTfomY3EJVaM3yCE37bQbqr5PxqnufJ14O1fj-RoSOxUc53HThCGImUHBzmBxw0qHnRMDtXUGh5rIFKB7Ye_BJQvGNZXNwwe6yKeUk9P2VZcFhobWgVuCjkgl-pER2ewYkddUS42WHrftjM-4bA7yYWPkFlZ3PaFLC8zlw7--7H-lNwTYg23okw==>  


Platform Parallel


Interesting parallels to the data-driven ad world appear in a Wall Street Journal article about Amazon's Marketplace which is populated by small businesses. Much like any disruptive platform, Amazon offers small businesses a chance to take advantage of its technology (shipping, etc.), but after a while, Amazon may end up jumping into a market and doing it even more cost effectively through its scale and technology. The app-driven marketplace is a push and pull between big platforms and the ecosystem it needs in order to thrive -and sometimes eat. From here, Facebook, Twitter and AppNexus are also examples. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZENM8bLBvkaNyetldDXJIvZEyfaazsXTL3_rSed8o8T-qVypHjZ75AxKaf2YMyVnM8_m61JGeQckpMHQjQPrHDQN4DpQwovo673S8cWTdWB_vwRXsKtIrzQhc4hM3zMt6Al7gvVgpArGIxuJb-__GhdpzZxgD6grk2ATGR1ILqwtKY2w1bCtbavGlI3UO3CzDuBNzGwqNH_XUnTIiePi64qhFyx7GzlX9y0uWYAyJ8A=> .


Adding To The Holdings


AdKeeper is taking steps with its Keep Holdings strategy and earlier this week acquired an email tool called Unsubscribr for one of its holding company products, TheSwizzle.com. AdKeeper's MaryAnn Bekkedahl tells AdExchanger: "Our purchase and integration of unsubscribr.com into TheSwizzle.com is part of our founding strategy to enhance the engagement between consumers and brands. In this case the enhancement is giving consumers control of years of unwanted commercial email." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZENM8bLBvkYbQCGAJyZpmlDAzv08L8oNt1k5isiSmI38nONu_UNrOQjLT1jHGv-zch2OJjaQaTuSjQmkOynWcrQJcIII0YSJdjKJiQLhumjd2ofV9RJIHDzbu8o-1Q1fVo85qANSpHDTHI2wc0To0MEsEwirclvu>  


That Sucking Sound Is Yield


The content marketing tech field has added another competitor as former DailyCandy chief Pete Sheinbaum has launched LinkSmart. "The web version of Get Smart," you ask? Hardly. The linking toolset is intended for "audience development managers and yield optimizers at a publishing company" who are looking to improve the user experience when it comes to link management. Read more about the company and its recent funding on TechCrunch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZENM8bLBvka_JkqbCy1ruy91X7u-8x9LfP6Y4uo1412wA7K7QOvLJh4ep0Gv1gLqqvzN4ZicYQhn6-ubi2kFOd63lv9ykCXn8mC9p_F2W8_MH8KEkldbZdajXzWElbZuwu0qznE3Yj5pqDyulo2usUai7j8ssNBx> .

NBCU's Streaming For Gold 

The network expects to net nearly $1 billion in ad spending for the 17-day Summer Olympics in London -- and at least a small amount of that could come from the extensive amount of live digital streams NBC Universal will be showing. Adweek's Anthony Crupi notes that at some points, there could be 40 events being streamed at once. It could allow for better targeted ads, as swimming contests may draw different viewers than track and field. Read more here. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001ZENM8bLBvkY5DIG3cROwKaestj3-VbAdp5GvuYBucm12tunRahGTHeKiuNCBzfJSk7si15RJvPK4g657Q4dnFdFk86zF1BmKkCn1pzC56wq27tfAa8MrauGdfZCMq3zdXwyuMvo5DVvOls9opSZYxa47wNGKtL1gybo1dANOFM32drwdPu9cKgCnUVC20ZAh>  


NYT To Open China Site


The lure of luxury advertising -- not to mention a growing middle class amid economic uncertainty just about everywhere else -- has led the NYT to prepare to debut a China-based site. Although the news site will be based in China, ad sales will still be run out of the New York headquarters. Even before the launch, marketers such as Bloomingdale's, Salvatore Ferragamo, Cartier have lined up to appear on the site. Dotomi Sets ValueClick's Destiny


That's the take from Piper Jaffray analyst Mark Zgutowicz on the negative impact of real-time bidding platforms on ValueClick's ad network business. The display ad company finds itself in "the precarious position of having to bid up impressions among many," Zgutowicz writes in an analyst note. "While it has and will continue to buy lower-priced exchange impressions to complement existing network inventory, economics here eventually go away as more and more exchange buyers outstrip supply." ValueClick is lucky that it acquired <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJawxoVaoQ0eD9RVjnFBFOoTBQYsZQhBGcLByb6ywpcW_JsB2QPyzMigM_2U5IFOaFSLxUok5AE7QJdvkUows9FiF0gvaLL6_SfqR3DFl2cTq-zGXFO98Epx0uajsXCkWKEmwvdeJYM9nHbKqfuySrHKq0g8S7QuHmW4SMLrfQ8miQ==>  ad targeting tool Dotomi, which is now setting its parent company's course, as the ad network growth wanes. 


Singular Zynga


Zynga aims to strike a blow against platform fragmentation (and cut the cord to Facebook) with a tighter cross-platform integration. Reaching users across devices and websites (including Zynga's O&O sites) could also bring ad value in the form of a unified online/mobile cookie. AllThingsD's Mike Isaac focuses on the diversification play: "If multiple players aren't forced to play the same games through the same platform, that means players have the option to disperse across multiple mediums - mobile devices, Facebook and Zynga.com. And that also means revenues could potentially be more evenly distriubuted." Get game. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJZm4AuU4yFDy3NZ0riTvGtsnXLgrBqlCSABSd3sCoh0Nrk7iskAW83pJVpK2vLtHPCz-WhJ3IjLLmQ1FtOjJQaaSeQbwcSSV-Qlo4TNUyN_XE6qvcMo98_h2Zv15vGQ1TiQgD5_XjP-Vor7mHdj2g6xTSRph2Cs-2CRMV2XFF_vbDKZcpbYVrE6SBI_QlHG_mDfZR3YQ87bkg==>  


Owning The Device


Entrepreneur Chris Dixon uses examples from the mobile world to discuss the difference between an integrated (where a company owns the device and the OS) and non-integrated strategy. He writes, "There is a trade off between integrated and non-integrated approaches to building devices. The non-integrated approach lowers costs, but adds friction between components that compromises performance." Another nice thing about "owning" the device is you can control who targets off of a unique identifier and who doesn't. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJZBJN9cW3K24hnsm2G9hb5b2Kygtn1C-pGuFJVzeBw7C13cHoUk_k-M1YQpA-RRclSuUdc2d8mZEhUHIgAO8M-jboIykjfxtrnFHhDYc6nnFJkYek7JaHZaFwJ8ltU5WRtafYKHw4pGMQlhwgR8wZEc_rUatWAkQ8l7tvkXul_ep0YvJIni0di46CjxgxoZxzWRXe4D3g2w2Q==>  


Cross-Device


Cross-device, rich media mobile advertising and analytics company Celtra says that it has launched its new creative optimization solution. The release explains, "The ad formats natively adapt to where they are placed and display perfectly on the specific phone, phone size, screen size, particular game or app." This echoes yesterday's announcement of "polymorphic" ads by Microsoft <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJY_CRxwB1Wbd0uZEUVXIydvnSCYzZMFKEVfuabdsBsTxNFx8oYlGCkkr73KzVobFMEkeb6HHEGPH2T7p9iNbrpf-PM6OyNDAb1xQGPE3cBrLngW1kssjz8V7rTj3Li9-stCokCj0JN_cy4ppB_eWvHE4JTekYEfz_E6DGb4CN9giNLUtGKEjU-7l3VNOBKofjoKN2IDyr-YniwQk-RzE0LVKndr1yT0A_nrHtiZQgLl1WX_FfgdEnj4ZJM69-4GqDvpvCJhpd-itSh7R2JHNN_vrmE5zsJHcOcrpduBzc-pT3C6GrygBd6Q> . With so many devices, easy translation to formats old and new is important. Read the <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJbY7eCh6ym8YzveDBNGyrsjERMLKt-rEkZEVmxNBOMYM2S4GwB-DdkgrQWnn1bFA0KHuJds3TCrkqDjC2-60UejiDn7ydgkwoWZmri7uxqYmqz8hrRyAIAEqmiz2r0I2Kspl4wei7KsaWqPvrGEPOLujap1H1ESFFGlocugHqf-44UOnBMpOoABoa_qnbKhTbNVwzHjeJz3qyg1C8YTJ7CT>  Celtra release. 


Biddable China


On the UM blog, Yean Cheong reports on the recent RTB Global Summit in Beijing and says real-time bidding is a hot topic. Cheong examines the possibilities of China becoming #1 in real-time bidded inventory in the next year or two and writes, "I wouldn't doubt this for a minute, if the enthusiasm and interest from last week was a good indication of things to come for RTB in China. Especially with the volumes of inventory available, this situation is not a matter of if, but a matter of when." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJaF3QfsHCOK_AXUqCvBccs6LTzRdhN_64rHnjyRqnGTPnKC_5cUcwP6NbyAeRg4MZUOPqX96EmEWVUPx8ikEDXO2aqp1vxbiDUuo-ovnOhq2z0brrVpQ7XOkxZvxolue3cJTItVqdXLTrQdNELYmC1CBD892K_td7gwx1dUGSyG8ww1nJBONGgX>  And that may be no coincidence as ecommerce in China is expected to explode - in a good way - according to a new study by analyst firm AT Kearney: "E-commerce has increased by a 78% compound annual growth rate since 2006 (...) and will reach $81 billion over the next five years." Thriving ecommerce = more retargeting. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJZ-4jkghof_1-fdYFXH_1TsfNEk0IoAAqaTK7kA_xjn-wjvvFaoOzGXVb0BvITLDFVa-456iPqkE73wHyMTceeuU33E5mQh9Ygz5SdZUAzhaZgUL474e93cLAEKrkrccPGIxLuL_Gjd6a8Aq8KxJyIXQ5-UA5A0H0YxFwsCejKjRQ==>

Project REVV


comScore released its latest pay-for-play ad network - and now SSP - stats for the month of May. Coming in at #2 in the U.S. as measured by reach was Rubicon Project's REVV Platform with 88% reach, or about 200 million uniques in the U.S. Get it (PDF). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJbgwNv4zm3rYWAUaO0GJlpOHSgPjg1Q-GZ8JSDO9kAhBnG6vHEO41Hi2Nk_2IJDfcCSdFKBZFtpLYFhjdJscGg5_cnTLuTMsO2AWlbappv4etp8um7x4NZksNNdnUSquwGJ0CXdZEJ1iFafH9_WFnQwe_zyuOaLdTDJmJXFh0QJee3UtMa5Vv8BnNRjn7gR17lICkKZQaIdRZkUwbmchtSLtDviVhwiqLXJhbb3Axa56Y904h8XnxDM3fxowEHOK8VItKMm58tS4CKOABSWSGL864XUGLGqYWcDHB5PKU9VrD7zpw_R4gRFDRru77b_Wtc=>  comScore says the total U.S. reach is 221 million people. 


Atlas Hugged


Facebook has confirmed Atlas as a preferred ad tracking provider. The designation gives Microsoft's ad server some fresh momentum in cross-channel tracking. In a blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJbk13DDXFGHtaq_Oy03P3pZ2kRmO3IGPIThld_GZNB3qEdooBR9rygf3nONaN2owfRlKCyOFlgqSsVfxbufezbQUf5pLXgKzWbDnaWZoZ5Qi4TyCgRNyr6VHukdWKvi_7qKBuLqkI-s9ZpqlRb3KOIVFaQ2k6Cx64XE1yd0eTVD9PdvHgX0S9fDPQNuQLNA_u4h6_zIy9zqb5XkMtcGjKzgflCSbztajK6v-vf1785npM-NePF2mur3OW3LJkDOu_n1pydiaaRRl_0IFRXdSyT6aPEKxPdweGA=>  Microsoft says, "Atlas advertisers can measure impressions, clicks, and user interactions on Facebook ads, alongside the rest of their media campaigns [and] can now even track through to conversion on the advertiser's webpages." In a Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJb5ZMER-mHoNlbghulcsef93cQmdie_7I39eRQ4vn_ZdIvLRnr6TS1U9XqKaD99lki8PVtBlwnAAM40v2VQ_eN26OE_ctrYq8cMCADa6NhXGfyChZhnifcQDf1GnvQtZ_-b0A_At6fgL4ZD8DLP0h_nt8vGhELnhlcTPK5t5BEtDQ==> &A with AdExchanger, Microsoft ad solution VP Rik van der Kooi says the company is "continuing to develop on the Atlas stack... We do that now through a partnership program, where other parties can add capabilities on top of Atlas." 


News Split


It looks like Rupert Murdoch, probably the last high-powered media executive still in love with ink and paper, is facing the inevitable: with the newspaper business buffeted by shrinking revenues, and the entertainment business as strong as ever, it may be time to separate the two distant sides. Stories in both News Corp.'s WSJ <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJYvLJ2sSuAuf__4SQveSIG8K__P0lBZAnOk6gcFXvuopgEMV_1y7KsQJCm5XEaeorIHU0_BLGMHYCc2KXCyei8x8Kt2UCJm6gmK79vHCdgjcg0X96UvrE4BdVgpWj_3jaqDPXi0Eo4Y_KZWpvxPAeU9dWuBKwBsnJJuCp8Aso-0Zyvm5sj-vAffQ8JFirWYy7j-OCTTTLbn5lv6PAHb_wU_>  and The NYT's Dealbook <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001KfrQXwkmkJZvAg_eUdf8CWbVDsGr0oFq9dm9fLwaxkVCEHQcANkor5pWLg7lmBc2mJjWf58tSoEat6X2Ph5ls-h9cQgGeid9Aej1viwtEgDrGm9OV_Ygf_7cTmdeVDugD776e8qwL0yI49W2ShkgCTNzpxNshQ-e8a--NHgJdD9ozU2Lk_U1LPjGE9OIK5LYwKtOF3RM8js=> , confirmed by News Corp., note that the hacking scandal at its British newspaper division helped promote a position by many News Corp. executives for years. So with newspapers likely parting from entertainment, it's worth wondering how long many of the print operations will go digital-only. 


Earned Media Tips


Buddy Media continues to crank out the whitepapers while the closing date for its acquisition by Salesforce.com doesn't occur until Q3. Earned media is the topic of this paper and since the ad tech ecosystem never met a Tweet it didn't like, here's a tip from Buddy, "Keep it short and sweet, and watch people Tweet. Our study found that Tweets containing less than 100 characters receive 17% higher engagement than longer Tweets." Funding Attribution


Remember that famous Tom Hanks line: "There's no crying in ad tech. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VISNjelV5ajfb81qmr7DRn0_qYPCNJYo5WGSDmGVD4rhgrsYeXkSBLfF1YL547LpgE_lPlvW03y6B1aDcXohmr309MRF8SSY11H3G6I_Jzrh9DGgHPGRMOa4o7l0bA69aGgmXyP9I3z5dPaXD6S7hg==> " As Visual IQ proves, there's no crying because the investment keeps flowing. The attribution and analytics solution provider raised another $12 million on top of an initial $3 million raise. The company claims traction in the release, "Visual IQ currently manages over $5 billion in media spend on behalf of its clie <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VISNjelV5ajI0JZV2kht436o78uyNCwq25iPsYUkYtlq5leGDKOqqKKu5L2dCgWjkdDOvq0CyAgHnXk0qTv7AC0D_wheygqsba7DCGks1SCgWR1II9Z3nK1Tim_Fejkl4iGK_SGxeZ1o0abUWm8182DfA8FjOFR1ESUg3tTs-Ej4aHHTnnudhxTxE5Y2VMci> nts, which include two of the top three national advertisers, as well as two of the top three agency holding groups." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VISNjelV5ag32BwARCRbN_8g4C54O86OkAEAe-wGIiRasUqNJ8ZAvLRQCdnDI_coztuIatA8RBrbEuOG0a2EKXn4_dXyDeKBH70UftdbKZVMi8llta0kzUXgEm6WvR0yHJJmx-gwDAvx4a1xoUBbLXt8apGDzs__0coEs0fZJakPULlXHQ5KReWFGgjpQ1iL2TcZzm6rNDwtxKCZZ1pkf0tlEhcw-_558QlkhxBhg_0_KWaPHC4MEUnQ7phtjsIrKasNylEN1fTPQxt0zyle0w==> . The quest for the cross-channel attribution Holy Grail continues. 


NYT Flips


For the past year, social reader Flipboard has been working with publishers like Condé Nast to not only distribute content from magazines like The New Yorker on its glossy-like tablet pages, it's been also extending the ads on those titles properties as well. The New York Times would seem to have been faced with a choice between open, ad-supported access and protecting its digital paywall when it decided to make all its content - not just stories from its feeds - available on Flipboard. But as AdAge's Nat Ives reports <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VISNjelV5ajjSSOd0TDu2XUgVhvFsFNRN047XGfWMstQ2w9JAE2dPrayh4PZ9HzY3BQPmAzzpwLxpOmyAgEspLwAeqt-S47HdXXPuNn3VP_j3Bn-DY3BrydRgfekhmx26JMM_MZgAnq9zDcYQaZ7JUkQtcTyUyap7QegeQ-aTtPdGNe2cnG8zfcp7gTJU1yRE26p8MEvwbZQyx4J8GuY6w==> , the newspaper appears to have found some middle ground, as it will be bringing its pay meter to cover its Flipboard content.


Polymorphic (Display) Ads


This sounds like an ad unit that Dr. Bruce Banner and The Incredible Hulk would like. Microsoft revealed a use case for something called "Polymorphic Ads" at Cannes last week. Microsoft Advertising's Jennifer Creegan explains on the company blog, "The challenge today is that launching multiscreen campaigns is too difficult and time consuming. Polymorphic ads are designed to streamline this process and help brands to focus on telling their story rather than campaign implementation." The idea is to make a conversion across multiple platforms easy. Read more (see a video). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VISNjelV5ahpmXP3ry4UaBV_a6xappM0pxB-3Ip0Ui4M1AkME3o35EjLrYbBqcH0kphZKQOIYvFb8lIthZVWhumev4w0WN7QgMVZJxgyGUpV7SOSl_XmWzwzMnskl7y9VFeiN5cPsLH2nk6uvDZNmYbGB8qUN8FbKoWIR_0AXHBpAQg-paWXNxZZDK5rGI5tOC0oo670WvIMEsZWgfVXUPgSjEl-R0mWQZt0aiFHeS2NaStXclIptF_NPXJVvcvjbLiq_7zl8rNs971bdem6AHv7cPzA5qc3nIQwwIwKDyOqVn33KtFqZqFkuLS6fI6S>  


Viewable Video


A VideoHub report suggests there's little problem with video advertising when it comes to viewability. From the release: "Approximately 88 percent of all ads streamed in the first quarter were fully visible to viewers, much stronger than statistics have indicated for display ads. Of the 3.5 billion video streams analyzed, 7 percent were partially obstructed, while viewers never saw the remaining 5 percent." I wonder what they missed. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VISNjelV5ai5uL93oDfju8bc-W5mf_r5X7mx2_J5v2QuTEJM4NGzqjcoGjLqNF_uZ9f94GHIQa_MU1TqjEJGsaxIjIWdl5KQvscn1O_Sw2h99PB0Ct4hXGISe8-zNcayEgt1eMf5WlP3mjL-fPJjZxEg7F9JZxqNFIuksXjjk2Tm1DgzhgVU81awavD-mUTN8kx8th16oo7RYpXk9QjM5yA1f_f7yuiIFACQeDct8a0=>  


Casale Media Offers SSP


What comes after a world where "everyone's a publisher"? Maybe a world where everyone's a publisher platform. Casale Media is getting into the SSP game, dubbed the Index Platform. VP of Strategy Andrew Casale tells AdWeek that when the RTB madness hit several years back Casale Media zagged to serve the supply side while others like Turn and ValueClick zigged to serve advertisers. "There's a handful of SSPs, but now there's somewhere around 40 or 50 DSPs. So it's a good time to innovate and bring a new option to publishers." Read more.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VISNjelV5ajI0JZV2kht436o78uyNCwq25iPsYUkYtlq5leGDKOqqKKu5L2dCgWjkdDOvq0CyAgHnXk0qTv7AC0D_wheygqsba7DCGks1SCgWR1II9Z3nK1Tim_Fejkl4iGK_SGxeZ1o0abUWm8182DfA8FjOFR1ESUg3tTs-Ej4aHHTnnudhxTxE5Y2VMci>

Exchange Boot


All Things D's Peter Kafka bubbles up news that two of the early DSP/retargeter entrants to the Facebook Exchange <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm62YDwpbJLz1oB_6agpJcM97ADD3wK9m79xyXooXKK7NFwJdmJMfE5nRziTT7liN4A-50WYfsm4-06YSDYI2zS_OEvhsVfOjm3e3YJ53Ff0-1VQIL4a7KYdmNqJ27KcfNBB683QPPGGNrAIIPsvoYmem2v0dqajGWS2vcOmqR2pvjxEwRuuvUJWZXcc30Wy5oVLABjZ1OsYzoKcYbqhW_6->  may have been shown the door. He admits, "Who got the boot? Well, nailing that one down is a bit tricky, since no one's supposed to talk about it. And if those two companies want back into the club, they're certainly not going to say anything." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm6nJELTkVCRnIltUeS6rgKYzpiJR8iT6GyPyPeAfUrBEkPjTscEzAdZnC3m67THP_4GrMG5Z3T9edRd-zw2cVjv-u1HzXQ_PStIDFxkZzClDjgq09TLiS9UNGlz0zI-tnyRh6ZqB6cujXFooxJdsByF3IQLHhqTxbY93R63YBaum5-FZt_CVAVG9C7z_s1uT_k=>  Meanwhile, Adaptly CEO Nikhil Sethi sees benefits to the new Exchange on his company's blog such as taking advantage of "time spent" by the user. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm4E3RWCcpWpROx_cC94Z5WeDEngqQ698MuQP9sWPnfAuf3SISOkdrkwg5PW17TS38Jd4NfkZ9J-1o9QzC4bSMuoWHTHeruT4n_431GlDsdsxwdnltbjrIWsyb6XPSUFedzS1lEruN8HSO7W_ksqjallzSnLuID8v1lgNfG175uWTw==>  

Ads Are Back! 

Ross Levinsohn tell The Wall Street Journal that he ads are awesome and that ecommerce is no big wup... kinda. The WSJ's Amir Efrati paraphrases the always anonymous, always ubiquitous Yahoo! insiders as saying, "Mr. Levinsohn has told colleagues that he expects to be judged on whether he can get Madison Avenue ad agencies, which represent the top brand advertisers, to continue to 'support and grow' their relationship with Yahoo." This is the same mantra that Seth Dallaire was preaching before he left for Amazon and before Levinsohn was given the interim CEO role. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm4YDleBfULSADGhWbSIX0pHp5wW-8HjP1wUOpoB_w4udXSCDbgB4W7OUgzsu1cnZSyDfVPQV24j5jBhcbSrh8G304lBXpuH2RMb16yFoxFGNq0nd82MykXvQujE2zBX5tfvpiGalntjtRW2rseYN_GcW4BTMaQ7j-hiH0-4WHctTXNlnZ7Wi0i4> 


Combat Showroom 


Executives at a recent Best Buy shareholder intimated plans to combat "showrooming <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm7gs9_PUh-JFf8h01Z9khkBwXUN0TN9NNrfwoL7uVSklcnSgAcWwCUuLox7g4CcS6oNkzQkUUtiixIdW6vKHeug1ZcAy7j7-iYoUNmEiD1F9wOwA7Vtf-E-fWYBLr0iGazYqYIl7jurhKESA8MO_tHGWvURt7Str9U=> " - i.e. when consumers go to a brick-and-mortar store to look at an item, but end up buying it online presumably due to a better price. Internet Retailer reports, "Executives noted that Best Buy was committed to better competing against Amazon as well as other online retailers, even when they offer free shipping, by offering a stronger in-store shopping experience backed by digital technology and services that provide consumers with virtually all the information they need to make purchasing decisions." I'm not sure that's enough. But same day delivery might be a cool idea. That's gonna cost bucks for Best Buy, though. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm4cZsGromYk2M-PlFvT05lmcAymG1HHcOmkegdZt-0znYowQ1WnlEN2zLKRtp33FkE307gahEk46FKD06RRpjKK-4JLs55MUqcv5OjDiCAgxXZh2rtRmIA5GRY29L-r3jN1iHEm6aRvV4isQBb6bo0MUnO8wByGa91G-Q5SZWIMrQ==> . 


Brand With Content


Arguing for digital content marketing (tech) companies everywhere, Outbrain's Gilad DeVries says its time to hop on the content marketing (or native advertising or [new buzzphrase here]) bus, "By and large, advertisers are missing the boat when it comes to using digital ads for branding. Far too many dollars are flowing into display ads, which are incredibly weak branding vehicles." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm5ocCMTDHXjZmC4gXCaPDk1yLM2xmr1pNOc3a41ld4qoF5WUhVdXBvENY-HGfdSuUnhvDz7m-KtUjIHAKdk1o8ovobI2uaE8sBHvJNallIetYMvCil4xIvBwuoRi6OZhu9ASeB9uzyTuJzmEhUOxbDp3c723dBQk5w9uvTx7fWh25-1Mwmpb_iQKZ_ZJnaB6OZoWuIZeiRvf5YMefoM9QTvGCdmH6FtHmc=> . 


Facebook Ad Network?


In what may be the first baby steps toward creating a Facebook ad network, Inside Facebook reported on Friday that Facebook ads and sponsored stories are now appearing on its casual games partner, Zynga, Zynga.com site. You can see some details in the Facebook Help section <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm7E0aPq4Lg1RdF9Go4m-yTML7ySuYrcB-E96RzfVv0ds2j_LnLT0fqIJAz2t-77gYii67fPfXF5YjDTELk6iiWcu8Ds_pVYMEON4VoJUzsN-FzvuQ5_wXbmK3XvOc5VqqHhCZ8nt_Fj5YaN_atE0jIn> . A Facebook spokesperson told the WSJ (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm5RDkdHLZKLrzZpOUiY3pFM3awr5szw5KAkYQo4E2CTVW8l1-d5YPlACKTrjIUW94w_JrREe09ACFi-DaJIFF5AhX3hPwOhmZDDlAIkK8NnAjxtCMUFBnyLTvkcCzcgyOSWc_XXP5lUnczFqINz9AeGOol8qXbErWVo08PxbNsbLLFZ1lDyj0sd> , "The company won't share any information about people or advertisers with Zynga and advertisers aren't receiving new targeting criteria." But, they are receiving new inventory! And the Facebook algo is getting closer to being unleashed in "the wild." Read more in Inside Facebook <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm5UshbY7x2WVtV_U5kIWq9wFwtna2EQ7OQcGxA-ZERBNbUlSpjBcpJyNDqkYG7oHha87zXqcLJkQnWIhsrjhX5DfVmqxVi06XC_vZZs5wdkkavkjtwl-vfkIe4w3XSa3x1ZGU6ULRX1UVP6mBS-z1b_AmYWOlhiwG3qBOtCstUBiSwIrYv7le2CbsUHuQWMAdUyXKgU7frOKLvRTUP0yIds_4J3VYDzb5GLIZQlB5zqXg==> .

In Sickness & In Health


Google CEO Larry Page's absence at his company's shareholder meeting last week had Wall Street wondering. JP Morgan analyst Doug Anmuth wrote in a note to investorys, "Google indicated that he had lost his voice and was unable to speak at the meeting, and also that he would not be speaking at next week's Google I/O developer conference or the company's 2Q earnings call." Google quickly moved to put out the fire as the CEO sent a company wide email saying, "There is nothing seriously wrong with me." Read a bit more in the L.A. Times. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm7DBnw1bTJ30QLYdbuUhYfoyJ1BgznLhJFB1hSC-h_oZ9YQSFOfY8ZUbNjJTB9aJH5-KTVjAMakv1fa_7eWDg6N3xwXTvein6rfp_dfAYjbLwjUCvE1xVCCktkNNeaUgfKo463CfFm4h1CgX_WuqNsuWujn_wixsP7zV77JVK1_BkbhfacU9ObwsgGR5f3MwaY6t9-0YGDurGw70UEHHfkrg4UoDe4GR60aBkAj8Z1zVYZC-xFQqEhskhnoIzKLxx-cpTdrtwudkg==>  


The Personalization Line


The New York Times' Natasha Singer checks out web page optimizer Monetate reviews the customer personalization implementation of several of its clients. Singer quotes Mahender Nathan, the vp of e-commerce and digital marketing at Godiva, "If e-tailers become too familiar with users, they risk alienating them. Personalization, he believes, should adhere to the conventions of in-person conversations. 'In conversation, if you think it's odd that you know something about someone that they didn't share with you, don't use it. What we're trying to shoot for is friendly, cordial and helpful as opposed to crossing the line and being creepy,' [says Mahender]." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm4dAz-Ylg09J0NaHaQeRwf4z0xcvHPynRNCDBHVxVXyhw56PQR-Ls28Dq9plyBeSzujeqaFTLVqMxDUYXyoLwaDIDAvDCTJLcB2_koOkzc_WTBjBRZmD_qvLTqXiHTqOs81maRXnWsbhRWiXtcWi6irrmXZmHzZI_oVUhxCVcl7PSmyeMzbh7RW1oetmLwC4xvP6fXpjNgbm2MpSyUq8yzywdq77c-dkzNaYwDR4np7lQ==> . 


Display For Video


More Street stuff... In another couple of weeks, it will be corporate earnings season and in anticipation of the numbers, Citi analyst Mark Mahaney provided an update to investors on Friday for GOOG <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001CICEdadyxm6j5p7zu1CJcF-uuK4jrbqLcFaiSIBHuXHFq5YXUNHHLfcgP-pUF664dp0OH7SwZnKThRL0fQDF_s6PFybT4DpUX7OKcspJ8oCwg5Q2vZId92nqynxekJlz1AcwJJqWTCxeqWljoTsyzdENUHbs4IroGFNpzXeb1LY=> . He's bullish and included a bullet on ads for video: "YouTube Ad Monetization Continues To Improve - Our proprietary tracking indicates that YouTube is now monetizing 94% of the Top 100 videos vs. 81% in 2011. Also, 36% of the Top 100 videos now have 3 ad units vs. 19% in 2011. Given this monetization momentum - as well as very strong usage growth - we believe YouTube is on track to generate more than $3.5B in Revenue in 2012 - 50% more than YHOO's Display Revenue and right-in-line with Netflix's revenue. That's very significant..." Video isn't just monetized with pre-roll and the like. The display units around the video and overlaying it are a critical part.

Brand.net Sold


Direct-mail, newspaper coupon marketing, and, yes, digital ad company Valassis <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTdznlF9r3q20HufI6TIEdVlyoul9fFoyqdZ5KqzzT5tvQurrRZ--oL8qqoX6g0YTx0OHdUprG1rgAVbSyC9yzFriAPnoPh_unZHx79Upt2-mw==>  announced the acquisition of online ad network Brand.net yesterday to enhance its "Valassis Audience Network, the components of an expansive network of online and offline data, state-of-the-art ad serving and targeting technology, come together." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTcIODnA1vkEozC3AP6cb_gGtFQzokqLZ_bK3oJB6w48foXsKL1nTIJjYJmaEDpOPhLxkQ9O0T_OkkAfOe2De-W26oQCsQ9k2EY_sfje9a3wg-mVQxpJe3btwjz7N19sLT1SM0rFp8na8HDfoCS7Bps-AA1Z7krCEwdKhnLX9xYK6LvZ0TkN-DnPXt1HR2EbfMU=>  All Things D's Peter Kafka broke the news, "A source familiar with the deal pegs the purchase price at less than $50 million; Brand.net raised a reported $27 million <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTfb-wTrtPqXvaHNr3ZRtZl_QItKhDQkGSQx-B3YIoyc8JROBFgNt_ab50QK_cahhdAI7MkhYEG_p-rgGe9kQRYtmoQv0WvHddsXdJHRTcDKkO8khCzwNOuT-UhxLVrhmsBsbNhNtT4cZgj9R8m02ci33clzUjc8pB3iEJdLyuPooEbBcGxsF2eIIyZ8cZTvZKtRfX06Q3NIiQ==> , primarily from Interwest and Norwest Venture [Partners]." And, read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTeo_Ux2B7PY2wX9ljYtuDRDFzL8fcbJ6okb5l36kLBGKRT8x5HAVVBdaG5tQsJ58wYPWXvHm63xxshQG8n6PA31wnmF3NMgeRhv3Db91xo6tSa0SMTJsuBMx9tvFPrVKpIzRSrl6R0jBcWTLBx-SaeTrduB-1BEdvSMK5OE4H-vgioB77_LRhpur02B06ip1Zcm9685kV7n8GeIRVHQYc944wcWfC0Hj0bsPOW99H_Suw==> . To give some context to Valassis, it has been dipping its toes in digital and display waters for a while now. For example, two years ago Valassis made a deal with Yahoo! to sell local display - see that AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTfS7oBZEbLUzaOVixX-pcC_dZs6xvtlhlIwflat6sbwn5m7iQ9ZV0cwLg86nZO5MUyZn0roZqqlO-p5aVZTsFPmVMZmFu_YoaT_Ot_LKvJBqbluNA2440mxolx9nknH37T3-dLmF3hxtpqCxvG4UnNw> &A. 


Viewability And The Sell-Side


PubMatic announced that it will integrate comScore's viewability product into its publisher-side app platform. comScore Validated Campaign Essentials is essentially the next generation of AdXpose <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTeHjJxhTuePF2sS7IFHpcJwm88tgmq6yRzCvvjFz5EBWDGHzALBY59ie_BYWZNDHCIM1oBaKu2FdBD5Sje4RfUpKYdRDno3925doD2Dazdud3ta7qu-JhfMhR3Ukoxl1bssyV-wOcio4Ga5d0aPrNvg6PNPOTLrF_SYR4SScm5r2g==>  (which was acquired in August 2011 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTfDmeDMDaHI-h9ZQcM_qrkW3Ugt20mxGMeWHFXqfzayzByQsTW_K_yyqdWeeT7Qsn4_JHTzFhwpKVcWg3xLI8HAJpAu647iCFuc2eWeEp_th8p1q_FHmj5CxGhy0FKgRS1n4s9_o3wKdtCNPlSi7ge1JOg859rhK3VJb7viU0evea0tgsJfglV2PgX9xkcU1oyrXEO58MDMvQ==> ) and other comScore enhancements. The idea with this deal is that publishers who sell through PubMatic will be linked to buyers who want to buy according to comScore's viewability-influenced metrics. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTdQ2-BHX32yJg3llLxOQoEnYvTTmwSIVhv8kPmZL6xbImGaublMydevslTUf2AzSuMMrteSpWPbYPXx-fEO8QI89Y-Q5EvB6A2UGMw2GGfj3Nbfc8Ll-XOdvbRlnUsZRqYxGZu7k-nUPg==> . The comScore web extends. 


Tuning Facebook Frequency


Omnicom's Resolution Media and buying platform Kenshoo announced the results of a new study about Facebook ads. Stick this in your algo: "The ideal Frequency Rate for ads across Facebook platforms - once a user has seen the ad seven times, there is a dramatic drop in engagement." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTcIfc8keWLmVfa9B3U_01RLCfn5GjyKQGjxACQGRfWEz25kpHPEf9AV_jFeohq_XBXzQsHEldIKmr91PWuVdLWK7Q74B460D0eeatH7n7bFZGIINcXizxApNOq9CWLhQEfetGWlaGfCepB1sJMMe-SZzo4u_CuswJLCGMqz9AQoC_i0fSyFhcPrv492ZTDqDa0RCecY8TCzaD30WS4tulO5kl43030RraY=>  And, download the white paper (pay with some PII <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTf8H7f1_SBltruK_1TMnpCgXK1d3Hj2MCYhF0gvQpQEwWZ7bXgo2vV61v-fVZ38CTP40ap58eOcYVjWsHC0vFO9Cxs8_lP3diJOR4l2qgN8ae0d2QWMzqC7r676ZguMw7cNILolkHN0KUg9sjB1jQxF> ). Another finding is higher CTR means lower CPC for facebook ad buyers. But does a click translate into real value (ROAS) for the advertiser? Ahhh, that's the question. 


Dropping The Pixel


AdExchanger was surfing the real-time advertising web yesterday and came across a few videos on the Google DoubleClick Ad Exchange and its real-time bidding protocol. These videos are "old" webinars and may have been around for months, but there are some interesting tidbits, basics and real-time, ads fun. Did you know that "AdX" has less of a match rate than other exchanges? Google says its because "buyers match pixels are more prevalent on other ad exchanges" and publishers don't like pixels slowing their sites and stealing (my words) their audience data. Only the winning bid in a display auction gets to drop a pixel on AdX - unlike other exchanges where evidently other non-winning bidders can toss in their pixel - says Google. View the videos. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTfYDNneFP9FNQrB4XeZJ8a-jlzzLfvBq4g1DQ-HdgiZlwqHjw6xUT6JKC3NpTdW7Rs7oMfcBcjP_Db0b9EYhsfZe_qad4db1UKTFYmpovleHFSO-cy24tp9IM_MmDm-Z-GfKFz7wKTujAMG1EiP1xIgFK5trrTgY68=>

Purple Power


In a post on iMedia Connection, Underdog Media's Jeff Hirsche is a Yahoo believer as Michael Barrett taking the Yahoo CRO role shows light at the end of the tunnel. Hirsch writes, "A smart publisher with this kind of clout can truly leverage opportunities in the marketplace. First, they have a chance to truly claim the position as the premier guaranteed inventory property on the web. With an effective sales force, Yahoo can leverage sponsorships, large formats, creative executions, video, etc. at premium CPMs like no other. The quality AND the scale are there." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTd_zCgeXv1PmIvEwUQG3AoASs-imZrdsauZnOQ8U8W4Sf0p44Zcl5eF7nuiaHima6AsRPL6vY1fl9gC2OpeEbVmBpIOhU7YthH6u8tsjZFMsOa5shkBiRngMaIHghVtn-pwZskMkqzF00rsiuqnGrG8PNj7sNxkkpXO7dsSLxYLASSJ-QSk43vM>

DNT Machinations


On Ad Age, Lotame COO and GM Andy Lehman reviews the Do-Not-Track machinations and sees a solution. He writes, "even in the absence of a 'magic privacy button' the combination of existing laws and regulations and market incentives will discipline companies that abuse consumer data. The end result? A long list of consumer benefits generated by advances in Big Data, with a continuing residue of vague consumer unease even in a DNT-on world." Read it all. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001sQR5jzz3mTfwTgrW78bMI_aQTFo1QOfbcMSAjnY_i2SRJESDvJ2Eor7k3mDA_DY5WKHKGyClzaDLjroWin9v8nk1xxwkL7rmeTRtarFEZO7HoNl_za6L-DVkWtiNPwoRJgQvaIPVOz-HtCzuj7W0OirAcJI6-OysIe_cZtua4BsS919ku7jEliZ36meaBINH4kgdPEnmiFYVju-4NrZBpw==>

Knights Of The DNT


Ad Age's Michael Learmonth says that ad holding companies among others have been reaching out to Microsoft to re-consider their decision to make their Do-Not-Track functionality default to "on" in the new version of IE. Learmonth adds, "High-level Publicis execs including Vivaki CEO Jack Klues have reached out to Microsoft about the issue as well. Both WPP and Publicis are big buyers of Microsoft ad inventory and handle Microsoft advertising business." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0Yzy2lRzyOj0s8Wm4h_T21iELFTnmtjpZwk00Z9SdYQJe47h61sx6qOWjRTCtsmFfp3fMfFV8NldPakHYtHZflbRGAmWW5-i91m6uTtuyUdmP2wzLlsC4yN7Dz6ZsuUm9o7fYIxtrwx6Gkt06m_jI4SLXZg0MRgJFAHc3suP9EpAdsDLuDIPMyLhXj3LjcvzjI=> . This week's W3C Tracking Protection Working Group Meeting may be a tipping point in the DNT discussion. Today's IAB Ad Tech Marketplaces event says it will offer live reporting of the meeting. See the event page <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0YIeiptmoXXMf-rXa-jFAB0I71SSPDlqLjSbi9eiyU6y17uxeQa-bjAcw0G6FIyBet1yefK3QruQp2rwdyPN3mi_szDFQon4RNqSwKxGGOHjrj8Z_zVXZh9L_PnlugfeChzCnwp0UymZXhdmK5BmUVVyaFq_wgMltlV6dxMYlMKDQ==> . 


Facebook CPMmmmmm


On Adweek, Barclaycard's David Goodman brings good news for Facebook ad fans as he sees the social network as a performance machine. What's more, he is in love with CPMs again. He tells Adweek, "The CPM vs. CPC learning is absolutely we've absolutely applied to [subsequent Facebook ad campaigns] where we might have thought CPC might have been the preferred approach. Learning that the CPM model and visibility and optimization that it gives us is at least the right place to start going forward." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0ZPCBgOCmmfoySczDNN-n7195f1t78bTl1KDY_6HT0KmREtlf9K8CdvxXcnxoV2LIbvkxKN6wBwXypkftda4d51J-QeuHx1gFzvWoCSGxcu1Iku_5fwbAF3M0N_Eec2cDxYfcJ5KKXswzr_nUVuFQ9ysTCre__vEFCuB8v0mbBYhkgeZATMgbzKGkDZhsrH0-B_mraV083FDDTWlw0U2WBd5D6cqgf3mvs=>  


UK Cookie Loophole


The deadline to comply with the European Union's law <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0bst_T9Nn7WPdauoIo4RoEDK7gcyVz6B0xRuaz2RaciMoU-3hgiByNZz0-0K_B9Ui-Cp3f6oqaJfK6G-Wz88j-6XmOMDrZFOyPjXGJ68ZA3yTEi3crkbbvWIqe6l6yJtprG4M3tG_5ggkUU1HLbiU7J3gMtLsHJgnBXFgx-nfwdFMmBGyZ1083n>  that specify how far websites can go in the using and storing of tracking cookies has passed, and now another one is on deck, notes EConsultancy's Troy Norcross <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0ZPJNmt8e3nDyji8Y7gW50SPNKXvb8m7gPVXhgGhn5rtioXPvukhM5irY7Mc-6Nb12fwntiwK3tXAsRtADNWTEnsnCZh9dAbR_ED18EmKGoDjKl8Sx5KPkVEk4bPRJ63KfvnlwROy-uiIGq2_aE2iJyj0NS9jbsJm77ah-MwvpSSNS42cwQsO7Q> . As of June 26, at least 35 percent of all third party cookies have to be deleted. But there may be a loophole: publishers may be able to use Device ID, which can recognize devices without interruption, even if "a consumer deletes all of their cookies, clears their Flash and HTML5 local storage the Device ID can reliably be generated each time," Norcross writes. 


Cutting Through Mobile Inventory


Common mobile advertising complaints: too much inventory and too hard to manage. Pretty much every ad tech firm operating in mobile claims to be able to cut through all the clutter and deliver the right inventory to the right targets - and the latest mobile ad problem solver is Todacell <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0a2-bdzTVQvuIQsVXeRNHQRK2sqZ2cyuuFVidXgE268u2VQSnhg_riR4eOarBcwRj944VyaL0Mk6yGzIIlqHNi8X1-USyuBUpRjszuTYdm9Ug==> . Whether it can or not smooth out the targeting wrinkles in mobile, Todacell did impress the angel investors at Afterdox, which helped it raise $2 million. Techcrunch's Steve O'Hear <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0YLJsYHbKujxRqRtZN2etGlFwhPuebtkmyECvcqVU8wU3GrePNSsAuRSlsYjogWU7op8NG-5_gqb2bM-XQYmo2HtSj3rPXvRaHnK9K3L5Mpuqtu4uWXYyDpSbYylpkw6ZjXPXDpyLIC6K8kXz6AVPW91TTA04Sedb7JMwYkyLUE_zi2H0kQmgGt0PM3SqPgmhpcmug-ckWoErUqrz6ddnofYR-bQuToBmxzRBnPaui3nw==>  has the details. 


Driving The Yield Bus


Scout Research's Matt Shanahan explores yield management from the perspective of the publisher who is thinking about offline and online subscriptions in a piece on his company's blog. He says, "Maximizing revenue from digital subscriptions is dependent on monetizing usage rather than the users themselves. Comparing print subscriptions to digital subscriptions highlights why usage behavior is the basis of revenue, and applying the principles of yield management shows why metered pricing models produce the most revenue." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0blSJqpdV12EKSOXvhxytcXU_7uGYzkUEPWqdD7DJceoFMOf9NruT3DLUvpAQUyxyuk2HVpVAhsm-Ug9rRQGqKPQvk5wuuWquSbs4RUhxnY3TAeVgylgDnZsJTTp3hOhr1x2hLNR3DKaCyO85kguMF_QccuyxR2yCw214AenZND8s9Bj781arzKc_qEBX260wU=>

Data-Inspired Cannes


Two very different campaigns won Grand Prix in the Cannes Lions "Cyber" category yesterday, one of them a personal data-inspired initiative from Nike. R/GA New York created the Nike+ Fuelband effort, which creates a single metric to assess the fitness of the wearer. "Data visualizations show where you were most active daily, weekly, monthly, and beyond. We created Bluetooth synch technology so when you finish your day, your Fuel is wireless synced to the platform." In the other top winning campaign, Sweden bravely turned over its @Sweden Twitter account to a different citizen each week. It won despite an alarming backfire <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0bzE6J2OsA9ddyeAdzHGhkTnKKp0kq2tIlvzETUzO1ImQycr7Jlhpf3fiF58cWwKZeKL-WiX-M9deFnDbSvTluLXIyuZ_X2KSzfe7lMioGkVVSi6PR1jrbDi2fLUyfIX36iMI-KuPfemTsjpihwZ_pB> . 


Email Data


Email service provider Epsilon has taken data from 150 clients and over 7 billion emails sent in Q1 to share some insights with the likes of you and me. Try this on: "Click rates decreased 0.5 percentage points (8.3% overall) from last quarter to 4.7%. Click rates also decreased over Q1 2011 (5.2%), but continue to remain established over the last two years." There's more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0bKyvKQAQODxurZc8wa15JFMxsdQwYIWq2L6fIdwZ3nlHYrizqj1CbK_FdHuvghPzCGMhh-YxwABDPR8H7YDaAn_2vq1zuDPEH4JaNkAjgBeco8wjCHT2Q4Z6vYDsSDiYrB9-umHQXCYtScZQQWfIJZDt9evQqif5FdE_-blSSWeJlhOIzNZwipOIJmPQXGRIxV4TB3zKK-U4saZLz6kJLaDgDex6_9d_wuBwnb39IhhA==> . 


Viewable Integrity


Upstream Group's Doug Weaver takes on the topic of the "viewable impression" on his company's blog. He's a skeptic and writes, "Anything that calls into question the integrity of the basic inventory supply can't be good. It hands one more weapon to those who'd like to slow the pace of change and the growth of the online marketing channel. We've been through this many times in the past." Read his proposal <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0Zz2XAGXaMSqLoU1AlOQcbB0j1UleRtzElwgpfLgUklhhAIchin0vMwHfCq1yHEVAKUGxG6cTrADb4CYuzVQpYmDWergwNox2zMX74NzUE8Y5xQXpN-QrtbsYQeDHrXSzndtd9urOE58g==> . 


DSP Acquiring


Erich Wasserman talks to AdMonsters about whether consolidtion is possible in the DSP space. He answers, "It would be folly to guess, but we see the DSP not as only an acquisition candidate but as an acquirer." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0ZQufJ1gd7pxHvH2rfw4Xumnpv8_O27f8NDpUpBSZ59-ANhPPkPApRbnpy4vvHR2w5NQaXCqnmLUaHJfYX_Mq8OiHjf-slDhB7e-61zNEXPi9fqVkS80OTiGOPJTPHaZDhsI95vHYZYQ9_4m82m7LiueNIOfbkvNqAOQXvHowIsaGAEt3yOeSI->  It would be interesting to see a DSP acquire an agency and pour the clients on the platform. 


API For The Platform


Need a "deals" feed? The guy that helped invent AdSense, Gil Elbaz, is touting the latest and greatest product innovation at his new company Factual (AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0ZS9ocrO7gP5-lKbkP3ZyrHuhSHwShcDGr7G7TTCgukchGG8C8Tcq-7Ri8yOnhtqb79Fr-s99epq_OetEyjuGJT_vgZtpOAhnrCZbEXzCKzHmlSarL1w2f2V3YUa9-aQgtMMS3AuNLqI_-9J42g3ehp> &A 2011). Factual has a daily deals feed called the Monetize API <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0ZjricbXMqgFD_-wmkAsHf8UFEiegq90uxwXOAFE3iDbRonMhft6ZpT18-9BNBNNQ20KPAw-2kPXLWFyL7GMLXao51NnrydNG9KNPwtL7QzZjhVyV9Uv6uLJPlh8d9Tqo8=>  which claims to enable "developers to snap deals and other engagement tools like restaurant reservations to any business in a developer's local dataset, and share in the revenues generated from conversions." Read more on StreetFight <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_4NrJ_2my0ZT9DcSQY6e8_ELvji89vg96qU6irtMmFHIQlxBqHUrbb8XEJbLqHQ4rmno5XPM13djrTPG0P_nf3jQQuZ-1qhhYZ71BgZOkEKP9G-4e5T2k9KFOmNZsGcTN6WCQhsKQUo9BVzc1lj79sPs1s6bk5Q-d0uNDOH_LObQMBTyF2RbOpTg7rmMxuy1Uw142lgQNlXBZ9ncS3-VKg==> . LocalResponse Hopes For Half-Full


Social ad network LocalResponse <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfie6ZQe1-tY5snyZzBOBBvW7j_Y5YfzGTAwGpAkJOjirKeGsrwsE7p3XVPq2t00Ub3noXq7qpcyiighe2gigpzovFsdkQCt6cJm9Jp4WebjwA==>  is boasting that it's serving more than 7 billion impressions per month. A pretty impressive number, though CEO and co-founder Nihal Mehta concedes, in an interview with Techcrunch's Anthony Ha <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfh-s57OQYGD-pShSauZnvP5IyX6rnEsD_T0E9ExFobnVRGsMVz-A80OnDcJt7LM71RBh2eQaIH_HQ5wNkhH16a_-Gx1UyB-heIEKa3oE_vO3vX1dhbayLQv9M12S3uNxcuMYtdTent0JPoZgeLEBDiyjFRfqX_F9G4=> , that the company isn't able to fill all that inventory. In fact, Mehta would be thrilled if LocalResponse could fill half of it, especially if he can still charge $6 per CPM. As for how the company is doing otherwise, Mehta claims the company is nearing profitability. 


I 'Like' Ads


On Ad Age, new Facebook mobile ad data shows that when it comes to fan acquisition campaigns, 'like' CTR is easier to come by than it is for the usual mobile display ad. Ad Age's Cotton Delo paraphrases Facebook API partner Social Code's data, "The click-through rate for mobile ads amounted to 0.79%, compared to the 0.148% average across all five placements studied: mobile, desktop news-feed only, desktop only (comprised mainly of right-rail ads), news-feed only (desktop and mobile) and the 'control' group (uniform bids made across placements). The click-through rate for desktop-only news-feed ads falls roughly in the middle at 0.327%, according to SocialCode's data." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfjOjVrP4ekW-pLZybdvQBYxNnukqiA_s01gXHR1BBTfaDAc5B2SM7IdPwH7XRBmtWnTLqHVe2cyRW0zSpfhH684dLCWEiE-YJOy11Blj-YiZcHXd4CYEn98IGX_WcHxBMY2zpPNifPHua7hSlqNjlp_jpl41B-jlG015Dz6GKwqoX1dFvo__ZP1faaesw8c-V8=>  


DNT And IE


MediaPost's Wendy Davis offers some perspective  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfgOE95dO4KY7aAncidOm2-XU-3Y0BY75rb1nWL-uJacd66jMY1eI9clm_Gl_5DL8c4ZsjOqcgzaHjmwxolp9dUeJhFk6FtYNLDhLTw2rgWY2YLGZlIitHpDEYOjp9b_Rgfw1RDVTcve5CxLsAHOHbZ2RExYhNeddAXDPqflWgyzFlXXI7j-sn2tRf0asq8Wo7Bk2ORYdxpwkYwLnV1_IzeK> on TRUSTe CEO Chris Babel weighing in on Microsoft's decision to turn Do-Not-Track "on" in the next version of IE. Babel blogs, "We believe individuals, when properly informed and equipped, should make their own decisions that affect their privacy online. However, we do not believe today's consumers are adequately informed or equipped to properly make decisions that affect their privacy." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfjXzoFg7tf6STee-w5W0oRZN4hwGOcKHym1O7D0PvRA17J4WppyGmzUmWEcO5T7zdGuIGYzD04cOVRkqdpzKkADpVj3x7ts5HFEWJxfM0KrBGVrZ49Og9kNWeKB7rIwuk26cIuWNrivXT920ujOxU69hRypg9ZdK1KAKj0KguBBmXdGIMCLZb-fhKspExR5PHT7pGDbhEAD_VVUmmV9F3XUrpDFWaw6tqzHuFhgCUAGy0dAMUnm0FH46QzTQnDBIDQ_7lT_wRKqzUqP3DKyYddarfrsBXW8YWVfIG85dBweHC1b7CieCFRmodycd39eThFvIiSzzFnAmUDxH78F00hvz5ddHswoT4oztfdTCfyngQ==>  


Video Ad Views More Than Double


Video ads were viewed a 117 percent more last month compared to May 2011, according to the latest tally from the comScore Video Metrix <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfioPikNG9atPuflAQPd6EG-wKZEdK1hI9-6gO6_tkX6nM4_FJdEQaPpnYOmobdL0mCFcEQsuWG0H6j2sRlqLDUUXiDd32_z7Ju-aMWLxBU5pQ1Ne_jutyKQUs2wbPHdgKaFREI4211WLZKNG-Z1yFwXZ6eTgIY_GOp89ZZElfhZOu_oERMfnXRglBkSkAbhjDk_ZsnBADruewA6h4YwBDeDQU9DEnMUu1xoHIPQjEbHmw==> . But a rising tide doesn't lift all boats, though most of the biggest players did see a nice boost, as the number of video ad views topped 10 billion for the first time. As usual Google and YouTube held the number one spot, followed by Yahoo, which also posted a decent lift (maybe that ABC partnership is paying off?). But as SearchEngineWatch's Greg Jarboe noticed <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfiGDPp5ZSk65VOZVn2juFkMXcStZDb7OnNs-TsaR6au327Mg09KDgrIAsC9a9hmfYjzf0ncMd4_zVVLPAJ_lxZApLqNi1sF0CoZsOHOzjcEYRq-Vtd2ctim7txO__CPTUQSqhgRvFfUQUALkw-tK0JpQ5yGyImvzon76IMlQ_1x5R9RJZw-LgwOw0NWzSJHLNQ=> , Facebook's video views were down 8.1 percent year-over-year. 


Targeting Apps


iOs app maker Fotopedia announced new mobile ad formats that speak the language of 'audience' to media buyers. Jean-Marie Hullot, who is former 'CTO at NeXT and CTO of Apple's Applications Division', guides Fotopedia. According to the press release, the Fotopedia advertising platform allows for geotargeting, user interests, language customization and.. you can target the iPhone or iPad. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfjZujJcMrZR_2xzS3oKOpRZiyLiPG863sV1gLI8Ejv68Ujgj3Ku01EkTz1PHGCvFr4jXnEqAcn7-Lhvm7GSP-CGVRgTCXts2yHOE8x6922yjscGlzlmjRKo6yHADI1BHIim6CyNB28oTppQFEHw01HgVsMAHhoN9HuHkbZ9snGPuwX-f-sQ07hVwVXxarNV3sxYaVsU6VGBVh6vYq2WNOs9sSNl3nhR694=> .

Analyzing Collection


Following up a WSJ article on Monday (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfglEv-B2OUOSMsQaV2fwXIXOlNUrN_bc7AlI5qxzw5v6lf37oXoOtF2AsXV8KIrsMeZ5GAcXbHixXM4j6HbSfpuWMC0GcRlNo_EFkfPxw33t9c9BRFOZSfEHClRrmdEPw6Ee0-toP-WVDdfMxJD6czyvQObwrr9JSiyB9GIY-VZKWkSLffQGyK1> , Krux has released its study which takes the pulse of publisher sites and all the data and pixels floating around. Not all of the collection is bad, admits Krux. Yet, data collection was up by 400 percent for the first half of 2012 compared to the same period last year according to the study. Krux provides publisher-side services intended to prevent data "leakage" of user and publisher data from client sites. Read the release and download the study. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfgtm8USDQQW4o1uFeAVbar1qNxnTEymahHJDIeaxbq_b7hc5qbJ5h6iOBR7mN_YvKo_IuLESPvHu6-LtDy_oXHuZB9_DTghD96tsMrE1E3vv8awGMU5rr2ghqBUASrBYklWjQdwJJOk-YuIJd-Adw_WsHpsJsvEYW4=>  


LinkedIn's Targeted Updates


Business-oriented social network LinkedIn is letting all brands target their status updates to the exact users they want to reach. The introduction of Targeted Status Updates is meant to let marketers expand their audience beyond their employees to outside individuals it wants to reach. As Mike Grishaver, who runs product management & monetization at LinkedIn, notes in an official blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfinSelSXxt9avppwn-aeHy80vZGGMp0AmthmPwOYYuro6ELSFQnlxLRyokHO1dx6LustmEanno9mZV8-5jDCfYdIad5JSIrOKM0RPDbW9WydshLqcDHh_55apg-e-HVLBD1YMwDRaBS4LfbG2nOxcAzPoo9VMtZsJg=> , companies can select a target audience according to company size, industry, function, seniority and geography. And once the audience is targeted, LinkedIn will track how many people saw or clicked a company's status update, how many impressions it got, and how many people shared it. Jonathan Lister, LinkedIn's vp of North America sales and marketing solutions, tells Adweek's Tim Peterson <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001mLiFvrMeJfgVQYOQkBY4OfIFtIDZj3qYWJzveym475Wrft-KRuv4XGJGEX5JPh_iGRsuq63s8VqDoJIakyf4sV-YASVGgj_VTfCQf9Xkw61stlti3f93gLzVn0ZQoyZvG8TC9XcqogC3mLVODbygeBbURdjXPiiJreQNGbXwM6sesLmRHqGx1-bfg5hqSQmA>  that there's "lots more coming" when it comes targeted tools and marketing programs for businesses, particularly in mobile.

Barrett To Yahoo!, Y! Ad Tech Plans


Former Admeld CEO Michael Barrett is movin' on from his post-acquisition Google role. All Things D's Kara Swisher reports that Barrett will be joining Yahoo! as EVP and CRO and "will be in charge of ad revenue and operations worldwide, including units in the U.S., Europe and Asia reporting in to him." Lots of interesting tidbits embedded in this piece <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYg1x4vF5gjNqgmKcJ_tn-tPgVwU4a8tp21jOWtAgAdqZ1szJV4l47sNxQuwpbSqyRZPdSMvDFmV3HttW-4RuURzl7qfLIv4MYWN4zL_MCYN9Aq8eqyaNhtTDBRNrCvRS-KfJuh4QoMnNmRvU8fBP5CeRyY_XVjeeNSHsD3HPgbFXhnCPE-Xfyt-pCknsFFvfrmHebggOYy0Zomc-uQX0tZG1vzJTMwPZhY0RT8nzrvBLA==>  including - Google may end up offering automated ad products to Yahoo! and "while there have been a variety of multi-billion plans drawn up by some to double down on Yahoo's ad tech business, that effort has now been supplanted by a feeling that the company needs to quickly get out of businesses it cannot win in or see growth," says Swisher. Read the official Yahoo! PR on Barrett, too <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYhqZdWGxgvNjnr_489D3SMg-2Ccl_1ejZAHlj0E2Uio97Xq6ieWzLIk71wcyZjFaFp8OubLLVn9wZ29xufJ3DQDhA7b2Z8BEL3Veq89ZcICp_0veuCcaUY8L0ZGsH-CwXhaA-0suc15aqQpf-gQV-VVCGa48UGgajLQDyS9f5FdqaytCF_ga6EapEtYboykeufQ9v1QfDqvk_vBOOXMgPXJo4-eJQH5v2z8TDpsMTwUWw==> . In response, Bill Wise, CEO of MediaOcean and a former Yahoo!, tweeted <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYjiODoA0hZS9ahkha9sQEGXvFRB-O7RY1M6J-RRseUg8xBhlyzyM40gphXhrKotH6C-Cgfd11sP4mMPJG4IpdXjFEatvlc6Jwwjsd4VjGp3Ef4sZNM9tfZ1gjyYaQrwWtC-Dz34g52HpLX1DE4VbHAN> , "Google's loss is Yahoo's gain (when have you ever read that?)..." 


Big Data and Ads


An article in the Washington Post highlights how "big data" is coming to the rescue of advertisers search for the "right audience." In the piece, AddThis CEO Ramsey McGrory pours fuel into the data-driven fire, "Isn't that what advertising is about? It's about the potential of generating action. It's about putting an offer in front of somebody, based on what you believe is the target audience, to generate the action you want." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYi0K_wZlYJpkdox_9O6U3-MtAH4nvogLNOI0H5uqHpc10M9nAVEm-a6E8RCVuxAUFoNrjco_CLIW3DLuk938Zc_XDOTcxpkNfULlgIqGgoJ_EMAtB36brbpt_U2XuXe9ndxFUzNgmaA7eDsF4MI51Nw3R_KjQ0gBag1Q0sp-gEz-cgS1yhUQ4hC01eYTGSqY6eMQj-3p-33HCrOABWqEnunlrSMKjC3p54YOtQpVcqpeVwjRdv_aXNlc1gaUDRjmke92vEAUDUVogpKtgP2M5-IGgr5Fm42bh44xW7gJUz2pg==>  


The Digital Difference


In a feature article on Ad Age, Jack Neff gathers hard evidence that digital not only works for CPG companies, but in many ways is better than traditional channel alternatives. P&G marketing chief Mark Pritchard tlles Neff, "'The ROI work that we've done so far has demonstrated that digital is better than TV. While you can still get very broad reach from TV, that to an extent dilutes some of the ROI.' Digital still has 'a smaller range of reach, but it's more targeted, and that's what gives it a higher ROI.'" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYhGElYjQp057Knp1fIMGk1x1f-7PrNBAsavsI0RSQ8lsJhDZVFDYmdpv4KdbYnCCX5LO1F6T5BMEEqWCW5_o_KlvbmxTX4uM3Y-WBnMjmM3mU5pWNxBkNXW-HuDtcWDsxieU_MygOzR2qar6lJzyaJCapthhHYrUfKK_PGiWH23cw==>  


Extending Telecoms


Australian telecom Telestra has made an investment in online video content distribution company Ooyala. Similar to Singtel's recent acquisition of Amobee and investment in mobile ad exchange Nexage, telecom companies continue to extend their tentacles and explore new business models as old ones evaporate. According to TechCrunch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYhCF6MFe0fT9OA0hpGyzYvbNtILyk-bwCFO37xK6zfZrsWEbln6zBUe53WXd6PGq4p-3exZrn4E0LQ3N-aKo2-46kHegJU4i73UziQLO0u5GLrvPR4HiBMwyYZljksc-AFr1WQaLunlgGGKiwAMfaAx> , Ooyala has landed $35 million in this latest round, which brings total investment to-date to $79 million (Crunchbase <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYjP17qYEUObT5JidWHQ9IvaAPiOognF7MXtUPlJFiN7TWbxKIVYD1aB6ph1MKyuz19LeAddoKaNqJq_QbagSSvRzdUh31yu-I98rVpwZNVTmUIyM3AmhIZ-oEERrzVqZ-A=> ). 


Tablets Are For Publishers


On the OPA blog, Online Publishers Association chief Pam Horan intros a new study on the emerging opportunity in tablets for publishers as the consumer goes cross-channel. Read more.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYi3YEWpM_C1xVi8vpT71doA3brgxm7xWtpY_j2GT9PsjPH6UkUFIxSj7rzJt8CyRtxXUE22EKKzlJipj5SNQuOYJosk5zX3QM14h62cCIQ45N7-EetnTGZQuonHRAxwbP3Mrf9m8gqfIMssIwcRK1X_qlUukAoa8IBp1c6HTwSm9EcIFfqc5f9l7oz56d07sYkBIKbv-5rUEKqNnq_4LXbS15Fj0ylIvTDmAs6P9CiT4npHmeBVxBKGQHoK_uKawBE=> In the study, "Paid apps account for 23% of all tablet apps downloaded in the past year; and The tablet app market has doubled with an estimated $2.6B spent in 2012, up from $1.4B in 2011*," says the press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYi0vRT4EQ0JhqNLD9KnqLd--YMVjKbtS9ODZquz85XQo9FLb7huug1frjOhejYT_hEc7oThOnddDFguKNOPJXDvauGD9lzeH8tkc84-CgH8J4BTxrjqYCJp8TqQIQdwpD1mijALzp8B5bpPtkQ3h12rJeZaBJCHuJpB1VRS8KMOWDUXHkhb_5dPaOscUs5qvKZi9f0sh32-C7YVX874LZ25tuN6fNjkOe96hT8maRdKPg==> . Get the study (PDF). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fokTL5yiAYg1xBR2q7B-C97RZh4z0VGjF-JtZT9LIHbF6bC1JFt8o24euQsGVRnqkcaLnT3nhKJTUPVUKpI0K_EHuGd7dKKWrGTvEM4GTR3Vl_-pJguj3--rTYBuoFFdsfze7hGEjqFFfOqsGyMK8unVf-LW9R0OQ5y8pXwBuTRDjfjqGT_lIDvQBtVYyKpjvuHJK8l33u0UqoPkM8GB_0WXaqinrOShrvmwAqwcSigTuPJ-UMKYkw==>

The Acxiom Database


The New York Times' Natasha Singer profiles the data treasure trove that Acxiom manages and continues to grow in a feature titled, "You for Sale: Mapping, and Sharing, the Consumer Genome." She writes, "Digital marketers already customize pitches to users, based on their past activities. Just think of 'cookies,' bits of computer code placed on browsers to keep track of online activity. But Acxiom, analysts say, is pursuing far more comprehensive techniques in an effort to influence consumer decisions. It is integrating what it knows about our offline, online and even mobile selves, creating in-depth behavior portraits in pixilated detail. Its executives have called this approach a '360-degree view' on consumers." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015yy4kn6VVif_THOMywfHvk9wYinspd8YKSzNSeZzFQLhYyWth4AynwpkiEnXHcP3K12Hdb2NRKfIAJ_0Redcqw5kUpHBC_g9jg7U_1d_bpImGQEHeLYkoOY3SD2b0gapD62iq3F9ZH7EM1usJA2XfuEz36bWEHUbCIUqR8hzI83wKKVlAzh41rJ-dDZvPgiVEGlGuxrM0XfiF25DK-rJC2-9x6uBqFqvmHR_IWmKMhk=> . 


Amazon Advertising


Amazon sales veep Seth Dallaire has offered a rare glimpse inside Amazon's ad sales strategy, including how it packages Kindle inventory with online display and other promotions. Local Onliner's Peter Krasilovsky covered his remarks during The San Diego Ad Club's "Interactive Day" event, writing, "The effort to sell ads and offers on Kindle...has been met with derision in some quarters. But Dallaire says it fits in perfectly with all of Amazon's other efforts. A recent campaign to promote The Lorax film on Amazon, for instance, got the full treatment: A movie trailer for the Kindle Fire, display ads, a cross promotion with the Leap Across America charity, and adjacent promotions for Dr. Seuss traditional book titles." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015yy4kn6VVieNMSHPnHdKMpfiX6-gMxp8nVN7kRZp3oEPKzIhJ8afxSPfwrxo-R3YFCVzAfBJoEV6EdTkqJw2Tf_KxS_VUP78RLAwpI8JTLRQjv9CwhTT8Cx4d0LtwuT2mfEkkqOnj44Fyx9LBBgbJMso146DQ9yfYqJHh1tokCr3L5Cp-RZE0nsqLqmw-eUB>  


Differentiating The Pitch


Criteo's Greg Coleman admits to Steve Smith on MediaPost that the Criteo pitch sounds a lot like other pitches: "[Coleman] knows his audience of marketers have heard it all before. [Coleman adds,] 'I say thanks for your time, and then I will ask them to promise me they won't listen to anything I am about to tell them. The reason is that I will sound like the last 25 people I came after.'" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015yy4kn6VVidjhQ5bfrqYdhxCnh7-uA_nuS9WX_IEkBCXH5fP8Eq-Vj5-GRt8Hd106x1Wl7Hi-gFPkDYOzLoLnN-5gIGPOZS9RtzZZSrCPmEFcpHVBpsLhr4f31juTwpeQnDj3uE5TPfOpm5x9WbF8jY0dOPMksrSIGOxdbpRzvwXtkNR-SqFlX90vpRR4ETdtid0KrVbIExKeB222LzHqjCA8A8-PFh0ZEkplVX3sw8=>  You gotta test -whether you're buying or selling.


Make Mine 'Premium'


B2B media owner IDG Enterprise is launching a new "premium data services" offering through its IDG Tech Network arm. "Premium Data Services are debuting with two new products utilizing first- and third-party data: Brand Scale (audience reach extension) and Target Scale (more reach extension with third-party data help, presumably look-alikes). Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015yy4kn6VVifbCCKM0wcYzjohLt6qrK_t7TwEKZyafkwVa3wYCiF9ettPkUTkciELSHlNypDHRdo-p0fPJSxu6bhY1Z1hPc-jhvK57YE-jTqJNF0-iH_PVWW0gRlVvUU0tiDxvMhW9N7fWLBaO_CTCaVNlILCl1x8C7O5p7uCDvHfOjOQf8JYQ7M4-SYX2-WlN_rYl0Teqw33SKFAkB9NPpDW76CMaZqE-6ko4yAhUswfapeeZLgrc_cIdZiGddsKQLvvKge2ygE=>  


Still Supporting RMX


Perhaps Ross Levinsohn is starting to prune the tech or at least aim at where the money is - including Right Media Exchange apparently. WebProNews flags <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015yy4kn6VVievJT3fhGRUykDLVhFYVQcPELUAM0asgMnc0qV4kGc_u73mWQjxE9sIROULQLXBdkYdRLoxTiWkA0nn-w5T76GZKJ6kYlZrObuhKN-GS1R9LvGted7rvrhcWVMGnqcON0F6SYJclFwgBzxcO9vaihONrxsvFunPP4YQftWOtHOIsQ==>  the end of Yahoo! Analytics for 'analytics only' customers. On the Yahoo! Web Analytics blog, Emir Kirrane gives some historical context and then says, "We will continue to support this community of Yahoo! Store customers and a limited number of other customers (e.g., Right Media Exchange seat holders) with the same Yahoo! Web Analytics services they know and trust." Digital Blaspheme Not Really (DBNR)


Using data from Bizo and Epsilon, Direct Marketing News reports that an April Direct Marketing Association survey shows snail mail campaigns outperforming their email brethren. From the article, the DMA is quoted as saying, "'Direct mail boasts a 4.4% rate, compared to email's average response rate of 0.12%,' says Yory Wurmser, director of marketing and media insights at the DMA. 'Depending on how one crunches the numbers, direct mail has a response rate of up to 10 to 30 times that of email - and even higher when compared to online display,' Wurmser continues." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015yy4kn6VVicnfJ8qIJ9ZIWiggrPbzQxQfOXt0cINl6BvV6YuR3wAY05h9ixYgSYooFkNFUJplA7Yh2vI-ThtZFp6ccuTg-babtkeChA0EgUkMxQ9-QnOmT7_QRY2jyusgxskgA_7D_1XDNT7aBIzyokY26MzRVsUJ7Wm7i3VKHZ2VnFn5c3v9SyK8aJ5l30pZkJPw99ipSY=>  But, email is 4X better than the snail version when it comes to ROI. 


Human Targeting Team


A team of Facebook researchers is dedicated to understanding the rhythm of human behavior from data on the social network site according to MIT's Technology Review. The Review explains, "The group has 12 researchers - but is expected to double in size this year. They apply math, programming skills, and social science to mine our data for insights that they hope will advance Facebook's business and social science at large. (...) Of all the people at Facebook, perhaps even including the company's leaders, these researchers have the best chance of discovering what can really be learned when so much personal information is compiled in one place." Can they take ad targeting to a new level? What's the impact in understand the behavior equation of not having access to an intent machine like Google search? Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015yy4kn6VVieDEBUh-QX3Ek6q19LA_wRvR0GC9-KBGE1lDuwaVXLVPZoRZqLbH3qD4EhHE6YzckjZVXP3zBLQJAdGl-LjpPJKMaNJQ8-_4dHx_djHPZdKqNc7FEeILJGbQmBauzuCrQXtc6kY9a3L5cmKK1sSYlpyEPPVYiSVZOHVYlaGI1lw9WNJJQDswcAS>  


Facebook Success Metrics


On the Hill-Holliday blog, measuring Facebook campaign success is the subject and the reader learns its not one-size-fits-all according to Dan Goldstein. He shares helpings of data and measurement, and serves up, "We really think there is something missing as all of these metrics are designed to drive actions and engagement on Facebook - and aren't designed to optimize based off a strategic business goal, such as increasing site traffic referrals or leading to an e-commerce purchase. In these cases, there are many actions a user can take that you can argue are more important than a like, comment or share. A few examples are below; however this list is in no way comprehensive. We encourage each marketer to better align social media KPIs to business goals..." Read encouragement <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0015yy4kn6VVif8nlK5dO6XQQhG-2nNAgOYAh9DIQyOoEtcn2_zGjnxRi6I3gRxPfv8CEQhDrokyR0eyfCDnxxd4XNmEWls4brebVGAOK4bzmoY5epc8k8U_wt0rP_8fcsKILs-vR5-L65cqsHZsdqkJRuUnG2ojJi97hE1iqMEhS5vU1bB8-D7OXUNB8ds6dSOhY-KppsfbJo=> .

Publisher Dancing


Former Knight Ridder exec and author Ken Doctor looks at Google's relationship with pubishers and says, "Next Wednesday, Google hosts an all-day assemblage of news publishers in New York City. It won't be the first meeting, but it's an intriguing time to be talking 'partnership' with news media. Why? Lost in the marketing and technology pages and posts of the web, Google's been relentlessly reshuffling of its ad businesses the past few weeks as it moves toward something we could call The (Ad) Singularity." What is that, pray tell? <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbwejSyI87EM0fGax6uPg0DHfNtzWWj6motbgsO8l3qQ4jCCk-0aw4xOHFom6ff_j-PrINuyjAnzg5G_ctjnRd0-vALF2cLQh226M0cCfN8s3W98yLw94nYjUr574yPHzaV5PZkvy_RHvXZdS0BVwFrPm6CyhdSFcGvPhmYQF8xeiH2-Y_g9yDqWmK>  He sees a "dance" continuing between publishers and Big G., "Expect that handoff, between technology and sales, people and product, to be a pivotal part of the next Google/publisher dance going forward." 


Social Software $$$


That bell ringing is not another angel getting its wings, but another startup getting a round of funding. Graph Effect (AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbweiZXKgPpJrt95O0P24zT53Int20eqUbkJeomdxYNSjXX5ivKAT7mCGCR1W1lmEBDtLCceCsreWNc4NNloEBzHN3nYqqMug-lp4zbQhvQQgYjwcjU0vQZ6uQpM7eXVfHD75Kwps8g5YUf973Xo3e8DHD> &A) announced that it has raised $12 million led by Rincon Venture Partners for what CEO James Borow describes as his "marketing collaboration software" company. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbweiXgK0VyIR5XHfTsYMlOvSg05Jc3PVZ0gcn_yQCz8EdLhX9o61dHQa-oZGZovOw6_s8VcEap8dj1oTY_OC8tvXwFqNKFoYdgNwFuyvQDdYjFzfxXnUISrIU8JMWs4J04C2EvqS8irHJg5T5NPtwwfVsa1qoyEEY3EayreQz_-wx0CqKdmbJpg2YAO00lpurltj6qY9c75bvbCT6IbxKSqHO5-pxEPAaKpdw8kPIgX0InQ==>  All of this social marketing M&A with profitable exits (Oracle/Vitrue, Salesforce/Buddy Media) can mean more funding for independents as their investors see the pot of gold. 


Xbox Audience


Tricia Duryee asks in the title of her piece, "Raise Your Hand if You Want More Ads on Your Xbox". To which I say, "How high?!!!" Duryee quotes Xbox GM of Live Entertainment and advertising about the audience available, "'It's increasingly challenging to reach these people, because they are spending so much time on our platform,' Honey said, adding that Xbox Live reaches roughly 40 million users. In particular, he said, gold subscribers spend about 84 hours a month - or three hours a day on average.'" Do these people have jobs? That's some serious "time spent." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbwejCjqXZU7hFaBSPVvBiVN2BBW8z6JzQRuOGoFYnoqT8OGUq-ogOD90yjzh46JP6ubreSDxE1u9iMcYvht87cIPKlHTtQ-PiTPiUClgxT90AwmKD0V7TRzrBOafACW447jQwAyKhTwC1wBQsVjZk_fMd7qexoXsbqpjlrkro3zlW_QcNR38LQ8K6>  


Consolidating Tech


In "The Valley" section of The Wall Street Journal, Amir Efrati takes a look at ad tech and sees consolidation. Efrati says sell-side platform PubMatic is a buyer: "Some industry watchers say the six-year-old Redwood City-based company, which has acquired two competitors since last fall, is valued at some $200 million. 'We see ourselves as a consolidator in the marketplace, and that was the key driver of our fundraising,' says PubMatic CEO Rajeev Goel, who declined to comment on the company's valuation." Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbwehlo97jC4VPV0PQVX9DS6806YOPXZb80hIjpAVwcE3CvWTg_L9Thg5UeU9x1D_FPn-b-2BM1StjyEHBFp4M4hNwPDHyc8sesp4xEjQs88nNzMMVbcq8n_SJlWPG7mdQEHLK5Yr51kZwhx69Mq0htXKyRD13z_sSAhBl-ftlTSnWaheF5ZBb8KvH>  


Agencies + Cockroaches


Rishad Tobaccowalla explained to the crowd at VivaKi Ventures event why the much-maligned agency model will continue to survive and thrive. MediaPost's Joe Mandese quotes Tobaccowalla, "'The truth is, agencies are cockroaches.' (...) Tobaccowala said his point about agencies' ability to survive was that they "cannot do it alone," and must rely on outside 'third parties' to help them adapt and develop new business models and services to help their clients evolve their businesses." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbwej6MaRIMJJkieGPhtwkzIHqM53SePJz-dujCF5P528Xd3sU_yyVlRO7PrNIuOMg0m6XAjzNH6NrGQtUqSZUMYoCTaD6qO0zgg_qkg0wLMYKQik0MuylHvlqOC9uU6K77C4tFhIWSEEMBubzNGlIW971sa46LX7rOkFaXfELwk3qInL5awZw5-d0K7j2XKmSD4o7t06yqsYcYNV0WJ0n1KkAK8DE47iaXeg=>

Tablet Stats


Attention, Tablet Lovers. Chitika has released new data that says tablet people love iPads, but..., "We found that 91.07% of tablet web traffic comes from iPad devices. While the iPad still accounts for a great majority of tablet web traffic, it has fallen about 3.5% from the 94.64% figure we reported in early May. The rise in use of non-iPad tablets is likely an effect of the increased options for consumers (hundreds of models are available), in addition to declining tablet prices <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbweidyB9ucwfCo_-UUekM9uei8uaW04iQpKBEM6bNdUMFNQKn4rUnujzpyk1xqZWhb6PxgpYroAzvh9rwubhm3LBTQUZHHvEX7EfoGa1A_vzpa2pwSGmijAqmM-lVho2q3u1umqNpNpKoThM1d5sL_DPde1NA_EMTDKYmJPBb_NjEBzf1aBvrObHVsQe9x6PZiPp0nklBu96EYw==> ." See the graphic <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbweh_czmI2CB0jgmyiCqopMLj6-l1Yf6MTpVC5dKGzzpSACa7NkbijS_f1vwuciqHxSJlGdl7nujCXfVJElfE0BVQqlNV6JZyngelSN1Mm-Y0gxxlTm7J_Y8xNQIzYpCOZcYEltSB6uRBkZJS4bfzHfNwG9zqGmDc3aZDJRIik1lwtA==> . 


Baaaaad Ads


Everyone wants to stop bad ads. ReadWriteWeb reports, "Non-profit organisation StopBadware <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbweg6yV30hMy8fKf231cB7MPMOIKLialcHGUqUhzuT4-HnfSaGnO2_maO6GN558qeKZz5LNzBia5ok-T2eUbfdwluPZ50lP2LT9FJwx6Tszp8CA==>  has partnered with the industry heavyweights - which also include the Interactive Advertising Bureau (IAB) and AOL - to launch the Ads Integrity Alliance <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001y7Q87kfbwejHT6tQSGTKh15POkbiYtRLnKpr5b79Jw9BwTg7dRiLDVACxW9El8ATMQeNh6hb0fpo4agH4z-9ukugjjmE_aZFYVv9TUv3EjH-2GnAz0i_gfllUn47OWi1> , which will work to educate, tackle and promote awareness of issues in the Internet advertising space." Retargeting The URL Shortener


Social ad platform RadiumOne continues to update its product line of data gathering apps as MediaPost's Laurie Sullivan reports on "'re.Po.st'. The URL shortener aims to not only improve the sharing of links, a la Bit.ly, but it also "serves up in a dashboard as consumers share information about a specific product, which expresses interest." And then, those interests can be retargeted through online display advertising. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BGjLjxsRr79_Wi4iKGGb3qaTfxnLmgg7A1rEXsgd9iV02Qo1lctO127qkA4Byo2wONnviGdIu7FQUrNKGHlc7TPU97xLwBK96nd0UCLrvFTKmx9xmwhtqFlsapJWQnKyxBedHyiNeSWNaronZnVJI2Joo8ACAkgDhE1hNvlhgxoXYcpzVrYTM2ij_yiOFqaX8cH2CC8V64pweEdgkI645MNhwsXtkHEtlE0T3JKqq8M=>  


Moody Ad Server


On Ad Age, Cotton Delo reports that Microsoft has recently filed a patent for technology which allows for the serving of ads according to mood - no mood ring required. Delo explains, "The application further asserts that the advertising engine could have 'monetization value' to marketers, since it could ensure that ads aren't wasted on people who are temperamentally unsuited to them." And so if a consumer wasn't in the mood for a certain ad, it might require a "make mood" by the vendor or publisher (OK, made that last part up.). Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BGjLjxsRr7-Ch-Aq_qMUE4T17cfyzxnczF8eRXG1xaDffLq1HPWXKN7ci_5-gxwWT7LoCgooyiorN_HeYqeW-rXdA9gsg9rfv5jKkI66yawRldUtS8rUVGXJu_i3yx9wXVq4L4V9qoGrjCbFu2sfS19YNP85bA31c3DezmhWdlwBqu1dwlFPEpBKDB00dqvakI1D3gWk4biv8j6qRSfomA==>  


Excoriating Excel


As a workflow tool for media pros, Excel long ago outlived its usefulness. Or so one might have hoped. Writing in ClickZ, Julian Baring says what's needed to finally eradicate the loathed (in programmatic media circles anyway) software is a commitment to standardization. "Ironically, the data-driven management and rising automation of online advertising has not yet been replicated within the proto-typical media agency's toolset." Read on. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BGjLjxsRr7-Luanlii9jPB8ut1Fz_cmbPspp1A07jqiivQ-srYs8FTDwL4MuvSzt6mRP8fCkyJDHS6RDaZ5QjpntlsKoprDtha5rULXpqyy1JWFElF-sYt5RF4IzDbn0bjgJWAcQTu2k9xSRhhfoP7Y-JrEjQbBz3hjNlskuSuHO4bbj7S897L8ezV-T3FUf>  


New Ads in Skype 


Skype is, arguably, among the most powerful social platforms out there. But there's nary a mention of "social" in Microsoft's announcement today about new ad offerings for the product. The new 300 x 250 "Conversation" unit appears during one-to-one audio calls on the Windows version of the client. "You'll notice the Conversation Ads are presented on a clean, uncluttered canvas allowing your story to nicely complement the consumer interaction." Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BGjLjxsRr7_MVmMW5Vm354LLOf3Mq7o2Ign9yHHhoa2uYou3M9B2OGlfWZcGLH_pXPo3hnUgQY_Qyx78wLYTSVQ1qOUKGz37tTqR1FLGWJTIyfGb59oXbvYQxf-iiNkkUjnik0JpkTOpwJ-lJQBvY4rCOMbTWfnZbIPI2n2LrPNKmAAiDhdPfbGFjTtQHtObTx5TkOgOZYRi_u_8B3WxPPL1LGemBL_c-nLGXen6xWQmoaSAPGP10BXnTTiUx_BAZHMHmujXJERuJa-L2K234g==>  


Making Targeting Data Work


On iMedia Connection, Rare Crowds CEO and former TRAFFIQ CPO Eric Picard prepares an opinion piece "to save targeted advertising" as he examines the consumer's and ad industry's interaction with first- and third-party targeting data. He writes, "Publishers and advertisers own the consumer relationship. Thus, they should be where the contact point for tracking permissions lives. Since we now have mechanisms for real-time sharing of inventory and data, I recommend that we use these to support the publisher and advertiser going forward. Third-party data providers should only interact with the consumer through the publisher or advertiser relationship. I'll explain how..." Read how <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BGjLjxsRr78zr7foMENE8rM_wtX6a9Gmm4HlFhuwzyhJIozQBC6hHA1CXV4RJ-gwjcKkZ1MFhNHo16t1up87IlXjfhXaYf946Wmt5gJas2DYfxpy8B9LSTulxB0ydqw07a25AsJjlzKLaNw7Si5I8w==> .

Searching The Data


Using aggregate data from client campaigns, research from Marin Software says that the CPC's on Google declined 12% in Q1 2012. This follows similar findings in quarterly earnings reports where CPC's have slipped with waning demand - or have been adjusted lower as Google looks to drive clicks and improver the user experience - depending on what story you believe.
