Komli Adds Millions


Ad tech and ad network company Komli Media has gone to the bank as the company announced yesterday $39 million have been added to its venture capital-infused coffers. Crunchbase says <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfOGrhGtvtv_BLTV4G4R1AAsjsIq3TEp_tpUiJFnfT13aG2LE3XfmECcj0i5lt9iiM9DXpWKSPQlwkOWGBiXc5VN1MM6bqbopGuutHw5tPnkQYJ4CEM_KECURrqIzXBEmFwHaqGXnvwhiw==>  Komli has raised $60 million all-time. This latest "inside round" was led by previous investor Norwest Venture Partners. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfN2tfOteN3TUuCv5wiLpBUVVc0H2_x7cCAh_PcTILW1u0Hs9MQxYCudzBySOvE4vRJO7DDCfJ82r-wSvFx0GkE2CuIad4xOKBZvcp1MYIGjGFdsWBNb3hmXnj9BxoIbg3QxDoymR0OBIALEPZd7Fgqi9LfP87LCV9705PTCv_mjaRALG-_3MoUNvBGgqawlaJsaa-gYe8cHO5-bkGS6fyK2cSRdVtXwB0M=>  The release's boilerplate suggests momentum, "Komli Media has grown 150% annually since 2009 (and) responds to over 38 billion monthly impressions, up from 10 billion 12 months ago." Komli's chairman is Amar Goel who is also chairman of sell-side platform PubMatic and brother to its CEO Rajeev Goel. PubMatic added <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfPjAlWTn38MxxqSyPzA-bfdzZfd8DloKAX2ajdW-YRYN81tgdxXnD0Lw9fstAeIoiYMfZHnNty0WpfwBfCIH3yqZiORGwWdS8Hgi2F9hirD6JQ2KtgCWu5zf3sA9r_3XuVINc0Xhgs0NZSJ_iPfMg530Eit7NpJvfLgMuU3DoknVQSSkYYmo_YFgWiO1Tj1LHP3JXCPwRAhIWg2_eNA4WPGEbPSiCAn6Ys=>  $45 million last week. More irony: Norwest was an investor in Admeld.


Now Partnering


Yahoo! has chosen to partner with finance TV network CNBC. Yahoo! gets some premium financial news content. CNBC gets some hefty online reach. The release announces, "Together, CNBC and Yahoo! Finance will bring an unmatched depth and breadth of content to a combined and unduplicated online audience of more than 40 million people in the U.S. each month (which is twice as big as the next competitor) and share Yahoo! Finance's content with the nearly 100 million households that CNBC reaches in the U.S..." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfNc9-TEzYm5d0Xi95pzGKNPQRsbxOLxPi41xX_7LQa6JWsAGqoCykKp2iL0jroAGir_x54RWV_OoG1eJbqYhLeq0DtO8CMq2Ymncr9ckWbAMJzEm8UHNihT>  Yahoo! the media company continues to take shape.


IAB Goes Mobile At Cannes


Instead of figuring out a way to replicate measurements and creative that would reflect the lucrative branding campaigns that are the hallmark of traditional media, online is still primarily a (relatively cheap) direct response media. Well, Randall Rothenberg, the head of the Interactive Advertising Bureau, does not want to make that mistake, now that mobile is coming into its own. So he's going to Cannes next week to host a mobile forum designed to educate ad executives and "show a great blowout example of great mobile creativity and what makes it fantastic," he tells Adweek's Mike Shields <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfN2kv7bpDndVKR0mrVyPbokAPEoDdVgX3G0TVX056W-ENvex3iSNCHcWo1OjoyiCo6VbvUFFnq4SS5Scs2GcGx2d88qKNa0YiEEemBrneimLRqT23PFcXnNRCIhDVaMkLuJGX-G-ozw50Lax51XOtVodBAXA0QSvDj6XC2JcxHA5uWg33KHTTd2> . 


Media Pros, Fear Not Automatons


The human element in the digital media equation ain't going away. In a Q&A with Havas Digital SVP Michael Kaushansky, ClickZ columnist Jessica Richards asks if the rise of programmatic buying means media pro's days are numbered. Kauchansky: "Judgment day is not upon us. The human element is very important to mine true insights from the data being collected on the consumer and media placement. It is also very important that as professionals we recommend testing and new programs or our campaigns will 'implode.'" The chat also touches on privacy and the speed with which budgets are funneling to exchange buckets. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfPXcneo_6LWXKmKknZf20nqizk69pNgGGWleqD2Ufmgg6x0KRqqGx_6j65A9BTm4tGQg66xptI-0Z4NtZ-1h9ZsetLAqqBP8QGpQ09k8-7h6kzTRIj7CUE22UlvqYC4IlPEEaa5fQSdRkH_wfKA6R1PQoPagmuxdfyCO6sLWsELyw==>  


Hyperlocal Goes Hyper Speed


Analyst Greg Sterling, writing on his Screenwerk blog, breaks down hyperlocal audience targeting by two vendors: PlaceIQ and Skyhook Wireless. In both cases, the point is not only to pinpoint mobile audiences, but to layer attributes onto their locations using data from myriad sources. Key point: this new breed of hyperlocal targeting may be a branding as much as a performance play. Read More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfMkDVBaWzj77qH-UjqYuhx73TCmhX9PsKpNYgf3xNDSMUdXZVPcepCLmUSNvE04Z0JmJydoWR-OYrQ-V9BSz45qDTH-kDv3Tux9EoCGAIOWzBPnyxIu_pk2URbNN3krFrkO_NZcGnY9Jhr5xk3xlBlFRydJWRQMhasdJalRl6cjz1prQj6kkKeYy6jx8OzID-vxvqOfCd7rvIs--0GWObWU>

Targeting Stress


A blog post on Retail Consumer Experience <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfN1fHYuYvv2S3i4kHfT2lh01DGyUY54gRL_bDgj8teM6DgTxKdmvDGy1CYb0ECbDnOybayHuvEar962KBw4E_JIzff5txwmq0CPSG3pUDviTl12fjUO5leloMdwwpn0LqdUnmXA2wlYz8ebQ6b2bTwMUwSzdqiE-DS5q20_4BwvZRWuoH7m7wI2QKrjwlMRJP8=>  says that in order to get a true measure of someone, see how they act when they're distressed. Extrapolating from a March Financial Times piece (registration required) about British shoppers, Dale Furtwengler suggests that at a time when most consumers are experiencing higher degrees of economic insecurity and declining purchasing power, people's true interests can be seen much more clearly. "Pay attention to what your customers are buying during difficult times and you'll quickly discover what's 'essential' vs. what's 'nice-to-have,'" the post advises targeters. 


Data Scientist Dearth


Australia's Financial Review covers the rush to find data scientists in a feature piece. Brian Corrigan reports, "Cambridge University graduate Richard McLaren moved into the newly created role of chief data officer for ninemsn's parent company Mi9 about six months ago. He came into the business a year earlier as its technology chief but says the title change reflected a shift in how the business viewed its huge stores of information. "'The acquisition and use of data is essential in a media business," he said. "We treat it as an asset to be protected and exploited to its maximum ­potential.'" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfONo7pK3FitMQFQMiEsR-ugpoccgr0IrrNQLZU3Gtelndaq05UyvXlX1DUF1A27NwcbKWT6XdfeSYwpJy2VcIkcI-qE5HVGmogQyR_Dp3PrAcRz_lz2m7fwlqsQ7NUQ5EQ0Cpw7ATNpFKkAet0MUGNcrzPkNg3a6bIBvDF11q-2fT3Zod8oSrSM>  


The DMP Is


New Visual IQ exec Josh Dreller opens the data management platform (DMP) kimono and finds what he thinks is the future of the DMP: "Companies will be able to use their DMP to warehouse and leverage huge amounts of data coming from many different sources -- CRM, web analytics tools, ad servers, search marketing efforts, mobile apps, Facebook pages, census data, and offline data." It's not just retargeting cookies. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0019wCUtheCzfPZy2ORtwRIRPu86fOqJV_B2AgO8U3TNcLzMC_pQ3NBVeUF0F9Nl8wWcY1kIR9LjtjI477n3LpNTZxNYw1dZj9krpoaIq3WIbdeAfniQR2WZl6tlKHzSeZ3_vZLDmQxAnM1FznozB9yiA==>  


Sharing The Data


Verizon Wireless is shifting the way it thinks about data usage by its customers. Knowing that many users are multi-device, you can now get a data plan that can power up to 10 devices. Imagine if Verizon Wireless started using the access data it has for targeting? Verizon Wireless's CMO Erwin Tami Erwin says in the release, "[The new plans] cover every device Verizon Wireless offers, from basic phones to smartphones, from tablets to Jetpacks and more. Share Everything Plans represent a tremendous shift in how customers think about wireless service." Digital Billions


The IAB and the number crunchers at PriceWaterhouse Coopers revealed yesterday that overall digital ad revenue in Q1 hit a new all-time record at $8.4 billion. The release continues, "It is the highest first-quarter revenue ever measured by the IAB and PwC and a $1.1 billion-or 15 percent increase-over the $7.3 billion figure reported in the first quarter 2011." The 'hockey stick' continues. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NebrSgGgGRx-cuI_4cvbCKNs_7PJitOpsbyQCEgyiyoYvYLkcRF0CGzbsCZ1c9eMhYwk5LQljc1yErSWxWWcNVhn3akrHGM7rqeXHKCaY-u4OebyrSx3RyKScamZAKhYhogksG9JAggpoGycR83QZVritu7utV18EWLKYBRTS57ppsG1z7cJPjnNTL0VZtXoc56jn2gYLBZW2smKP2gtdNDs1xqWj90Q>  


The Battle For Ads, Content


The Wall Street Journal depicts the fight between Aol and a "dissident" shareholder, Starboard Value LP, as a litmus test for digital ads. The WSJ's Keach Hagey writes, "The debate highlights a fundamental issue in media nowadays: whether online content supported solely by advertising is a viable business model." Read all about it (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NebrSgGgGRx0BJNVOGjg_vwhUsw-VAfQ8-Cwl60V1nQQE-z93LqdtXAnhh6RMLJEb0sAKPpnOoqqM1_EF7yX_78QAPz-V9OklhmbwbvIfO9Av8oLCI0DaSd4xMbQS6A2pwOZIq4yEJOZCEVfnN5dWMiO4fA0j7qgxZqsPS2SJIn13BB_ye1VvHy_hXT1Wwfo>  


Saving The Mobile Ad Network


Mojiva's Mocean Mobile division has launched an update for its mobile ad serving platform. MediaPost's Mark Walsh quotes Mojiva CEO Dave Gwozdz about the problem his company is trying to solve with the new rev: "Over the last year-and-a-half, we've been approached by an increasing number of online ad networks saying, 'Hey, I'm getting so many pings from mobile users onto the content I represent. I have no way to monetize this stuff that's becoming a significant part of my impression count. And I'm losing money." Read about it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NebrSgGgGRx2wJao5O1ly_2OwkvAAooDy_R4Bbe9LC41XC3A84ywkUdZKWcLYkKJLqw4ENzQdc4Wchrd13rDb0kQC048BuQPRtm3rii702TzmKpaTSmI_Cx8QGer0J-qfRZxkOd_DYwuE_FB6EjUt4ChtJhYu5ayO0XQ_aeX9vvYItf4TtYhF-7AGQdBilviiFv7agyeO24duuHMkvmtpfATXKlDVToR1WLbzYRmZyE=> . 


Be Young, Not Old


In a think piece on Digiday, Charlie Thomas, svp at Centro, sees the necessity for everyone in the ad ecosystem to become kids again in order to succeed. Trouble is.. not everyone is into it. He writes, "Our industry is experiencing the young and old stages at the same time, which explains the feelings of turbulence and uncertainty. In its youthful state, digital media is creating an evolving, chaotic environment with a wealth of unpredictable possibilities and new ideas. (...) The challenge is that we are also an aging industry, particularly when it comes to ideas and systems around paid media. These mainly center on efficiency, which forces creativity to naturally take a back seat." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NebrSgGgGRwdI9f_sMYmJJp1qOdIKHKEP7I5GTfm5A5rxCPsJFLMBQjktXktMcqvb1Bl1VE2PleUemMs0Uf0dH6Mcz4fHDhKuTbUS7fiDCvMgbW6PQ2RMemuempp6CFLwUT02GXgU2eUpaInh4lVZI_Bhi6wxQDP9UgLv_rEccUh6V8f8a-gXQ==>  


Rich RTB


Is rich media better in a real-time bidding environment than poor/lo-cal media? Point Roll says "rich" is the way to go as it digs up some data for a post on its company blog: "We've found that interactive expandable ad units drive better performance for branding and direct response campaigns in RTB. For instance, in a 2011 study, PointRoll rich media campaigns that ran across Demand Side Platforms (DSPs) drove a 75% increase in click-through rates versus standard biddable ads." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NebrSgGgGRwMBvypII9az968oWpVeqgBMBAvNbxWxOCsqvujRQOigpoNril08l0fL_0OxtmN9TYkqOfyM3eQRotQJ-25uWT7MlX0Of46I5lfvn_-_Zpy0R2WmwJ4TIJ_r352U-42z0c33pZkns1jyDsFr2vKbCeyAdw4czD7AUckyfD_b5JyVQVhh0bdU9E0>

Apple's New UDID


The Wall Street Journal's Jessica Vascellaro says that Apple may be coming to the rescue of mobile ad developers (my words), and presumably mobile ad networks, who are looking for a targeting alternative to the UDID - or device ID used previously for iOS targeting. Vascellaro writes, "When Apple plans to discuss the new tracker remains unclear. But developers could receive some clues next week at the company's developer conference in San Francisco, when they are expected to receive an early version of Apple's next mobile operating system." Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4a2pKL6qcjxsFGmhE7OQME8YKV3BPMcWY_kYAkDixNjIB6u3t7IY6A4YCISXwTny4s9elTPp-edZJK0vcIFA61vQOV9S1OgqV7ln3qi7OuGYktSCKwgOMWLqPjeK0TP6m5G-W5tFFz6PzJZYBw2PiQ4SzzUSXz29Vz14y6Z4hnrl1eNiakhQ5jgD8xe2KFDcXo=>  How this will relate to industry initiative's such as ODIN <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4YdJ_PvGzRUs__jSFCysYKmNwTIII2u3L3c6A0FHOIu-TwyMYGVy4rWQjlutb3jpqcH1MsRmCibWRMeDZszOhSZvpwgnl8HpH0nfkAOZ6_-BJD3VYoZJn2Bpb74G5kqsgQ=>  remains to be seen.The NY Times says <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4ZCgIR4aO2jc59JSa_AO6Reef80x3o077Zn7P-_tyXFLfznns1SE0hf608ejB2S05REnfxErVXxtgjcta41pCe9yJMcePpwtqLk1Rgjhvg1kmBv9XFSWMzpUcKT3KC6sAdk2IQ-GZZfFr1BDVjn4WzKspX526EhKqoeErW8X-lXzz1mhyoa_OWWm8IKMJhQ4JreZecvQVgHaCyw3ES9Sf30>  mobile app developer are very dedicated to the iOS.


DNT Contingency


On iMedia Connection, Tom Hespos talks behavioral targeting (BT) contingency plans if Do-Not-Track is pushed through to the consumer in various ways. He writes, "You should be thinking about what your digital marketing plans look like in various scenarios, up to and including that Chaos Scenario: If Do Not Track starts to fly, and is adopted quickly, how does that affect things like targeting tactics and potential reach on your brand display plans?;.." There's more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4alGEBG1dd0ddajB_zvvYGtIxfZfdZB4C0pOAapXSmiZBSejU4yVAW-WDI5q_GU7RvIvMdGkbw8NTODvRUPyXrDfz9TQFTi7TIXbixEf33heA7_iDdZUGS1Fv6-Ln6ED8ogWQYwxhcnM0QedxCmNW_urzte4SpL07WnDzoDw76pebMse5We0HsZphEegf9LD3Q=>  


TV Ads For Online Daze


DMP/DSP Turn is going to take its recent on-air investment which included TV spots in "Mad Men" and "the Pitch," and create a case study about how online and on-air works together - or not. MediaPost's Steve McClellan covers the news, "The ad will also air online both in video and display formats. Turn has created a hashtag, #Turndecisions, to encourage a dialogue about "split-second" decisions that people have made in their careers and to track social commentary about its campaign." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4YcFuU-TftQul7BkJOvU5_TXj3cMM6BJ68J5K07ejh9_dWg27ttC8I7hObtDLLVtfRQeeFwWlEdpKzWnrjN8L4X6X7JGhwrSCuk5ijqPxBQtW7dk3b4CMvaofCdxOmDNR8Uq08siGnlAIZLVRKqWQY4UJ_UJUD42idZtJiyL89gjuzduCYCl6pdjC4rOY1M-3VYGmP6l6kq_GDw33vAScZjNKvRiQGcaiA=> . Undertone has already hit "the Pitch." Interesting to see online ad companies reaching into traditional media mega (but-somewhat-targeted) reach. The message might be - "online is ready to accept TV ad dollars and offer similar brand metrics." See the Turn ad on All Things D. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4Z7ZeopDUfEJojUKpkLL7mgmjjFsukNwc_TuIEz-R0J1o1vS6RkFiKk_n4uWU7u46YwYoGmWzAjFl4Q15AeVH8OL96bPdlb4jfejgg8m8G3a8HQxMsz1PZYolDv5cL4DfCGvA5TBctQiRXrrC7KwpQrIAx25vo4yBC_cwr3H5UP4Udiigm6CFNf1vSaqJAtahVcHsL1RKqVZA==> 

 
TV And Online Display


Russian search giant is making deals and pushing out display ad products, too. The latest, called "Digital Eye," is in partnership with Publicis' VivaKi. The press release says that "The new advertising method enables advertisers to differentiate specific segments of the web user audience depending on the amount of time they spend in front of their television sets." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4Z9G6P6mi38RCzApSevSfYrwhHzPsedv8p-2FtAxWvF5Dd6ur0mcRyI_CZ23zvfG44JOwdZ0w7T1H2j90P-rqdWxuQXX6OB-9KrmDbI6V4fdL_1ZdMJI4Zfw6Pwz69jlxeON4iKrm-oA6IQ_r3YZbcacgr2pQFXDrzK96DK2WAmtKH2oNsnwRHG> . The 'secret sauce' here is unclear, but the release goes on to claim the benefits, "Those web users who are likely to have already seen the ads on TV will be happy to only be reminded of the product, while those who are more likely to spend their time online rather than watching TV might benefit from more product information." Meanwhile, Google takes over as the default search option in Firefox for Russian language downloads says The Next Web. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4ZqcKaSFfp7NusPcKnpV2N39qZxbJbu0W8Pj-JCa794aN4t-VIXv1cHJtDLbtkTYDQ20rhv0-Rramd75zgMMfbpHuf8eS_Os76F-imVaEzv05lEs3-DoqInWeNCPHAdWsrJHjJ3WcRoTVMXz_DZWawzyboPTq-vC3lFCJ8OgsAaOKtLiF3o5Ru0ax9JC37-sk1VSUw_4fnlqmq5C_JGammSTeudsBcuOnct2Jxl2cPclOfw0gCsk8oFX5Ngakdr7CA=> 


Choosey Buyers Choose


Forrester's Joanna O'Connell along with Emily Riley and Sarah Takvorian have penned a new research piece titled "Selecting Digital Media Buying Partners." She sings the praises of audience saying, "When making selections, look for nimble partners who think in terms of audience, not media; who treat data as an input into planning and buying, rather than a postfacto output; and who deeply understand channel interplay -- and how to take advantage of it." Jack Marshall covers more on Digiday where he quotes O'Connell, "We hear agencies of all stripes talk about innovating for the new era of marketing, but the reality on the ground doesn't always match the vision they espouse." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4btbwWAJhHxvx2GWYh-UC-KdDi4sZYfO9yUsGs5aXj5aO0v8ndsihlcS8a4IBSPsQzt9i3I9n-d3xP1l0DP7BRto_xZJyhxwzc7ULf44GyCKh_vv3ZEb5xV_d6al1RQR3kbNVUoA8TIsH2NWZPa3KyU54UWR91f3DS0greq2xbGWw==>

Let's Play Catch


The former CEO of Nextag, and a former CEO of Orbitz, Jeffrey Katz chastises Google in Friday's Wall Street Journal, "The company has used its position to bend the rules to help maintain its online supremacy, including the use of sophisticated algorithms weighted in favor of its own products and services at the expense of search results that are truly most relevant." Read it. Meanwhile on the Google blog, the Company asks Amit Singhal, svp of engineering, to respond. He concludes his post, "There has never been as much choice online as there is today. Over the last few years, we've faced competition from new players, including social networks, mobile apps, and specialty search sites. All that competition is a great thing for consumers, it gives you more choices and makes us work hard to deliver you even more relevant answers, day after day." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4aidPlJhHn76oa6AuvXF2JILAm7qRT5_IY6ztellfc7uLZg4qLv8SWMmEQAvS0l5nNMQPfVJkYyxSXBeAZNii0JaXBs0oKLIEapl1fZy8fY2jSQ7tRzdThWc9JEpoehSb24iRFS5Nt2wBYcztq_E9BhhHKrdWs6wCrcSEzdvJH43iZ78mpXFNeBZYfRb5eJHmy6Ec6uruE0Ng==>  


In Support Of Facebook Ads


comScore to the rescue! In a post by comScore marketing vp Andrew Lipsman, he says that, hey, those Facebook ads that GM apparently didn't like - well, they work. Lipsman writes, "Through our research, which examines the impact on consumer behavior as a result of media exposure (i.e. seeing a brand message), we are gaining critical new insights that show Facebook earned media is having a statistically significant positive lift on people's purchasing of a brand." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001oYgiQmnlf4YVyTZTLqv2fsu7edcR3Ub2fzNKrqC31g1tFui3iCCNMvHdpvXsYm1oxA_qY0KOogT0BRkWwVNnmSH4Z1I7KY8PX_synajq0lPR3eUtqCQMmnOP-7gRbFB39wsfHxtl9dMYUYqgiISYJF4cEiQKgbCweDzNHGNr9Q5OwDNLbdRwcr1UbTF2e3NT3Z02JASe_Xs=> . comScore says it will be presenting the data at this week's Advertising Research Foundation conference.

Commodity Convo


Reuters Jennifer Saba analyzes new revenue data for newspaper publishers and sees ad exchanges as the culprit. She explains to the neophyte, "Advertising exchanges are electronic platforms that allow buyers to bid on and purchase advertising space at drastically reduced prices. Many websites -- not just newspaper sites -- rely on these exchanges to sell unclaimed advertising spots, known in industry parlance as excess inventory. The thinking is it's better to get something than nothing at all. But it also trains ad buyers to expect lower advertising prices." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsUq0oNcwDVYzNCXDljwxBbpk-2zOtuwVgJSaCBeAlhyQWU3GxaWsAGfFPGIgEHAOO_UxZmWoeeunaXaRn42ZBJVMSxnSdVLW5JhZ-fTtkf_5lrbLITUUV_1o1l3bKfaRf-vLlboczWvEnxo0-6byjIPACfZxHveDaGCqmCa2BTCpCCwfQVKryHtgmeLTTae9NOQKV11I5fJAg==> . 


Retailer Risk


Citi analyst Mark Mahaney shares his notes with investors from the inaugural "Advanced Retail Technology Conference" put on by Bain Capital Ventures. He's thinking that retailers are at risk given tech innovation: "Pressure from Google and Amazon Mounting - Retailers are at risk of being in an "800 lb. gorilla sandwich" as they are squeezed between GOOG (product discovery) and AMZN (purchase transaction). However, the IT talent at many retailers is one-tenth the talent at third-party technology providers. To keep pace with AMZN, retailers must partner with third-party technology providers. The source of competitive advantage for retailers will be to leverage their stores as DCs, create a more engaging in-store experience, and develop their omnichannel platforms." The corner store still matters. Read this AdExchanger 'classic'. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsWVSoynT53zIAD3GtifVn4VNP0g6pgcDGHUnn54EvqtnEYZuR8xQXTaS71g1S0cUNQ-yqvUdpvbv6chUFu2fTIYfvluPgckd9AV4PVPWOGjVsKiOASxIwNkK5TYiBxuSK_ca-ZhaNWqPnea3cFqrqgnz7ZjL-F1T4U=>  


Slow Boat to Mobile Commerce


Mobile shopping gets a lot of play in the press, but a Nielsen survey finds it has a long road to broad acceptance. For now, bricks and clicks are where it's at. "Online purchasing was rated the 'Overall favorite' by 59 percent of those surveyed, as well as the 'Easiest' (68%) and 'Most convenient' (68%). But people trust traditional stores the most when making purchases: Bricks-and-mortar stores won the highest marks for 'Most reliable' (69%) and 'Safest' (77%)." Ogle a chart. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsWvsCqvTjurU15H-VPLY642dRhrY9i2y5M8FgZ50eK2Y69o92yl-fjRkQRH26-S_sgCJt42cNHpzgSi0ANPM7YvzIVBvCIyGiT9cnF9S06iK9Ks15l-wOwQrsPcDYoPtXkDb4zbMpw6J-etHALetFQKA-k8jTjWmv--DWuzcFdMBd9DuapXXMisLawHnBggAo9xHqD8NJAamOrGUh7cOnIvkTNf-mchVCdFZHTeVtPIMCNq3_HdbdCG35kyMcYOick=>  


The DNT Ricochet


On the his Krux Digital blog, CEO Tom Chavez reacts to Microsoft's recent DNT move in the browser and says, "As an entrepreneur and one who loves the early stage start-up approach, I like contrarian moves, large and small. To challenge the order of things in such a public way shows chutzpah - my hat's off to Microsoft for making a bold move, whatever the motive and whatever the outcome. As for the spirited market debate, Krux doesn't really have a dog in this fight." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsXkXwmChl1J3EfM9pcXOVUK_ogoMdK_j5T4s79Qgs1SsV_qZbxbgNkZch_u__p5P6M1cb1OZJ9ESQQVvjpt1OCAhVhFPsXPp-Wua0L3d4iVyfgCgGNg8WhC2dKobCRsuz1EJTqCyIEPzNxPYzMmASpRms-8Ot9_efKMOXsWl_XftA==>  


NYT Supersizes It


Over on the Online Publishers Association blog, the New York Times chief advertising officer Denise Warren talks about the site's use of the OPA's expansive ad formats - XXL, Pushdown, and Fixed Panel. In a Q&A, she says, "Readers have responded incredibly well to these units, which we can share with advertisers through rich media analytics that provide insight into many different engagement metrics. We see the XXL, particularly ones that incorporate NYTimes.com historical content, perform at significantly higher rates that site-wide averages" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsWRuI4IcWl5-P10RuQyQziGy2CfNvLtn60cvWttpw1FqOBJz16ahTmD1L9vg1mOGUldd5_oLu5fzvJt7nwk_MRBvET1cLIobMastb4Jp6d7Z9ZXzjEy9Uv2wvdVWjyEPBfHaN96p-N2s3zkQaHvr2wjX8pLr7qQstkdR6vtyc7izg-gkYIMjWzG9fgYRjt_a80CY7DkXroxLqFrtNIVfGIq5EdCO94-tQRRLb6hG_y8IfTSJilcWx1b>

Movin' On


Satya Patel is packing up his product bags and moving on from his role as Twitter ad product guru. He's formerly of Google and Battery Ventures fame. Eric Eldon relays on TechCrunch that sources say, "Twitter's executive leadership is looking to separate the ads and product teams more fully, with each one getting a new leader. Patel's options were to take one of those roles instead of continuing to run both." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsVFrY2YgwxXgd9ziD5worqA-QiwHyaoShBtX-HcuabtheyGkVcbd4VaZKqEUtpoFJwfTzbqWtps8NttfJWLpckIbYWIWAnhc9ad1p2dwD0fD9tD-pfRiGgq9g6R6pZE33SlBCmU-e_4R_mclrLOY8dyJ3QyAxbSnIDJBSXUy2byCoOJTdX-WtrtVdy9HKCnQeiL5Q5OPGCJLsQydwpp2tb9WnJrk3RMyGv-pij5jvwq-w==> 


What's Premium?


Everybody is talking about the need for premium content to turn the web from a platform of cheap direct response ads and lift it to a TV-like level of lucrative branded placements. In answer to latest cry for "premium content" by William Morris Endeavor co-CEO Ari Emanuel, YieldBot's Jonathan Mendez <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsWKHgt1JcPIIfJ2F9srS4IkG2SeYpMNed6Hs2_OEAZEtaYoPgg_7sTs71rfqWKe6TPEmAiCVydPIPkyG8c-hS1txqH2lAJBR7Z0w5jKni7SMsky2zFRXn2iRtUtvSqQXxCq-4W6w1mR-k_DxhXUoVHnWPb2D-inQUAmZtKiKC2uag==>  simply says give it up. "There are only two things premium on a mass scale anymore - distribution and devices," he says. In this age of where performance, not premium, matters, publishers still have "diamonds and gold" beneath the surface of their properties in the form of data. Improving their audience data is the only way to preserve their businesses, not hopes of "putting the CPM genie back in the bottle." 


Funds Fly In Social


Advance Publications, the parent of magazine publisher Condé Nast, has invested $10 million in a relatively unknown startup aiming to help media buyers better figure out their social strategies. The company Unified <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsX9PVaUZxtkJg4BQCz0nCxCRAvKCVjI8Qd5iXr6ilZ85bgKTRyPVgabbCNp573KU77FeXtZcvVhGp8v34PyNEKWC81v0tsD_hvEPyYMplMTJg==> , raised a total $14 million this week, reports AllThingsD's Peter Kafka <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsXQYmV4IBGlsSBiLcQV-dz_NWWbTlNMD79umNHkFWOOgOgFMc5HWG3kWXaN4Sdtrrdb7HdkVhNvsOq_R0teNK2JS1IT4z7t_0DCG5wOgLXfcWg1wrFYJEPqXFqfDnxF3BkQzQmvRp_yleibInTMyU2I_eDFfYOC4-CEjXaKQWqJVirHYZDBQBwU_JklbH17iaq136nWLczjFNpoTgZbpxNgo4UERDpsqRKXyS4ByOAJPWRhjQZ1QyjjdKXOfCu8AQXYYiarKY5gDQ==> . As the print business weakens, building up new areas around social could help Advance drive digital revenues more quickly. Separately, Kafka (who has been, as Marv Albert would say, "on FIRE" lately) reports that the Buddy Media deal was very nearly Google's not Salesforce.com <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsX5LeeNPC1SJvHY68pCWfEMiviB5GvTuH7IuW82hsjKahGENMg5cCgSHfNqQKh6NRZD_fAekXXcawKtEZMrHgSSyAPWwv4CjDVXn3Lvemw6kZ5gaYf9U-xOxyokHfKfiYzNejb1e4UGlxMFkFIMs4gK8d9kDPgNqC5qt2fAJ4aHunRWsNXjpyCc> . 


Two Screens Is Better Than One


eMarketer repurposes IAB co-viewing data for TV and online and you people like to watch two screens at once. The eMarketer scribe writes that in the survey "of 'media-savvy' consumers, almost two-thirds of respondents said they had used another device the last time they watched live TV. And overall, those using a digital device to discuss or otherwise interact with a TV show preferred their smartphones to either tablets or computers." Get some charts <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001czWUGyWwbsUIczOYBuwoSUo9pSRnX_qIe2T6JQlvw4CVK65KHiWeRL5rSodWk5S2pYYh1suDooTivTMaza_3aH7ezOBovPTUtLFEPGa7lR6l-El8dQSL0vhKFmxlqpcv92uRQt1JXqO4hFYjq-jXFQ==> .

PubMatic Banks $45 Million


Sell-side platform PubMatic announced a hefty "mezzanine" round raise of $45 million as it looks to build out and, perhaps, even acquire sell or buy-side tools in preparation for an IPO. Peter Kafka interviews Goel about his company on All Things D. See the interview <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-ycREP5Geyo7wymr9yEcB8jciopD_lUsoF7xGgWoOy27QAt061u2LT3qflPY746_WNoQLfKmd82CGDf1fGj7PD0iRImslaabm9njuQYRzWb5jODv9cHHr4KNcDtyiz1cqCoBfVBAcbXKeYiHsKZ0vbkjBCVmyj2L9S3zHnFMESGTOLGIC8tXE46AykKF9_qTMq5sCmAITmxXzUbyT6fj2vOogcCFFm_Ekc=> . According to the press release, "This mezzanine financing caps a period of growth for the company which includes year over-year revenue growth in excess of 150 percent." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-wQVFIsAMTMkeqTapZP4t6C7QfAWYHLbN3czeujQ5gvTC5II9TLDozH3xRx_TIUSXzMhxVa91b5PbnUG2PVG24Wi8hBTqACQWRO3BHzUWpjGxk3Q8zPRD4a74EoTC3ZHhOklN7Ls5qwvVOe5zvbcJlcW7MUTlwoJuFAMWe3ufzyL4SGSfI9zzDSk7klMIhpcwMEhJ6n2hU8ki1uJg_aE5-E0o43UKQAbOg=>  August Capital led the new funding which included existing investors DFJ, Nexus Venture Partners, Helion Ventures and Silicon Valley Bank.

The company, which bid with Providence Equity Partners, has been excluded from the process..." Anti-trust? Really?

Privacy Peons


Cory Doctorow, writing in MIT's Technology Review, wonders if we're all sheep grazing the privacy landscape, kept in line by so many ad platform sheep dogs nipping at our heels. And he argues Do-Not-Track is ineffectual. "There's no built-in compliance mechanism-we can't be sure it works unless auditors descend on IT giants' data centers to ensure they aren't cheating." And he sees similar problems with mobile data collection. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-zyc0z9ayQHN9VhwpiINptPTtAGykYCY93rDCG_Yq961QYMJqsVcv1GozXQLdhuFPQBXf8FK8r01yvH1vb_l-FBkUzlHgpRJkRoJWoaa0W_ZXfdfxg6qG-Rn0w3JnsPMMrubXEE2W-brbBtdENud8e-SKjvKiwRA_TptpeG1zDOP9XJVq9etn5tvQmLkrqyuK4=> .

Spending Growth Through Simplicity 


Financial analogies are no longer de rigueur in online ad media circles, but Adchemy CEO Murthy Nukala embraces the wonkiness anyway, in a post on PandoDaily. Nukala compares the online ad ecosystem to Exchange Traded Funds, and says the former could grow by 1,000 percent over 10 years, just as the latter has. To get there, he says search managers are moving away from tracking hundreds or thousands of keywords and instead grouping their search buys around categories intent. "Savvy search marketers are now organizing their campaigns around their consumers' underlying intent instead of keywords, and simplifying their campaigns by 1,000 times." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-yq-16Hoy3bbHYAUPYBg6r4_naYOEb4zqlMBN7LAlW3MkR50vz0lKbKYEqQFnXlys6YFahHyEWO4kqOdhrGNbBPaEQydmQGJEA-_sxcvS-Z6b8wVzIqa4WOSiXuurgBRjbrp1--bc95m5HwxOoWDWi0_m-TNc-mCVB3tMLqsHfhin9KWTpyl3hqvBiUFtrjq20ni2bsvdd779zB61a7VlsDukWGOZdAxvI=>  


Microsoft Gets VPAID


Microsoft is reportedly backing away <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-wn-Xe6eBPUmPuow9pyJ24Q33mkJW2sV8AAEI51kQiDZrqKJIAjHUECtyEJDwsvB5N7m-uvfNErDCQOG1es5UcAyjp4XcT-MuX8DDSO6PKSzNhbHlYFmTqlNafbNyhvvoS0OeO94pXnX9K_2J2WGbVSn7Ibn5b8JCVQ8z8pVokot-f2QoBGfC4FGDfTl-nmLx0=>  from serving targeted ads via the set-top box, and perhaps, it's because the company looking more closely at concentrating more its online video ad sales. In a blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-wkj8ErQ_lual0Fh3JH7DVcGdCTjQ-0M7K2fr7sLHpNkcdqk1EFRXz0P0pyHkZw3iaVccDo3aVbTuRF2t2AQcZlSlMTfnjlKc_iW7MJRpw6pkWBfBb9yuMRrrYf61tBVLzfihLwD6uJNTO1h7_JhcOjoLNctVAaW7ImHd80TRTiRyRa2Y3hb9og3l0MCi150z-rSeRTwxPvqEDCqjbfdjAXg-GnPb6OOqIKbbBjdKB1B6wwwbcoWxeWfLOjC4Ke5s_ASjgZFynVRUwyYUDnP2ANtfwzCEdx6GpHaJEbXBNYlg==>  by Microsoft Ad Services GM Jennifer Creegan, Microsoft says it has enabled VPAID, the brand-friendly video ad format endorsed by the IAB, for inventory on MSN, MSNBC, and the Microsoft Advertising Video Network. The move reflects the interest of the portals, especially AOL, to focus on the low hanging fruit of their third party ad services as the owned and operated sites within attempt to find ways to compete against Google's and Facebook's growing display strength. 


TV's Loss


We keep hearing that consumers are watching more TV than ever before. And we also have been hearing that people aren't using their DVR to skip ads that much <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-zXzhBe5BeFMAIWzKzJV9IxmsgXp2PeT0RkJN5VCsd_5knmMNReHE4_LgaSL1EKXTNxbw2Wc5d32cgoB9g2rRJ6KepjhUXagX_eDrfQ3pS9wUUbdl_lYgvugydoJyiRkoUPjBzq_eSMYzkM1Pkc-yPwUC2Kio3lN6f8EdvV9CMxIYh6i9QktXYQS_XHxizBPA-vDiUrA9jJt6t4hbeylMs7ygA_puUpTz_-hxvr-np1IA==> . Well, VC David Pakman offers a more nuanced view <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-zA7el3EHjOK8QYDex9JvtKxd7K2z1LtECCs8pRqJctam67FQriGzOPn3sjtH3QD8bci6KFdHlNs5KbY-_fiMArrL_-qVYJqWCP-fR8tkNXTcUIy9GSYM2BKCFfntQWyNp-ggIFliS4L0W1i9JwVYWO669_MIFeW3iqabS_ZZNHXR6Fi_LlrW_jevHiGkOGwKwzS6U8vPlG4hh4cEhLqW2x>  of TV viewing and advertising these days, saying as we avoid more broadcast spots, "Advertisers will begin to spend less on TV," particularly amid the rise of IPTV viewing. Inherent in that is a why online video will ultimately dictate how TV ads are bought and sold. "Online video is becoming so performance-based, that advertisers now can pay only when someone has actually watched the commercial and not pressed the "skip this ad" button," Pakman writes. "If you really care about making sure someone sees your commercial, online is the only place to show it." 


Scoring The Page


Sharing platform ShareThis announced the launch of its Social Quality Index (SQI) as the company hopes publishers can use the The release explains, "SQI provides publishers and advertisers with scoring insights across 27 key content categories. ShareThis has developed a patent-pending, proprietary algorithm that derives a raw social traffic score by evaluating a site's share data such as outbound shares, inbound clickback traffic and page views." This sounds like a way for publishers to measure the value of their pages - which has been a technology gap that many publishers have continued to harp on. Eventually, if it's valuable to bidders, it could be part of an RTB auction. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-zypK3-mYmhKSnVuqWpXe_R3FNanqqiNAh6jDnAHEG__4xO589xA21EXAX1i7Z0HeANtWfck0gC1rW6idW9foO_ADlmCS2pEmyl856m62AbZOQasTQdFEw6FvTA2K_Pv96LyiRXrhvxj4g_f3wZ8xMGsRXQGfOuscbJVXaXuPhT2rLwyBVZqWe87rcIQYe19Dqn80cW6NIJm1U4Fxph02D7gnDy4jIuB_l3gunTQTW_OtoPROR_axtxOxIiGQIn-D4=>  


Retargeting Nightcap


On ClickZ, AdRoll-er Adam Berke takes apart the pitfalls and opportunity of optimizing a display ad retargeting campaign. For example, he notes,"If a retargeting vendor is getting compensated and measured by clicks, it's only natural that they err on the side of being in front of a user more times in order to get that click. If incremental lift is the goal, the vendor needs to tread more carefully. A lift-oriented strategy will focus more closely on the average number of impressions prior to conversion and prioritize exposure during that period, while tapering off after the point of diminishing returns." Cap that frequency. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001w-_DhQ5fZ-ytSh0kCHoXCpBYJQrt67iNafRIEIj4TYpwWBH8Qu8_r1jTB8ohoQUhquNpfTF7bJ0y66v6jYurxjKPQmkeijnSBjMulZruWGj6OGRfn8XG5r_HQVoldYMnDZceIo9nEYGoCGPeNCtQWZNVm07iIG31OEtX_LS_MeFfPBK394teh9oqm_qNAkoS2jE1ZDBc9Fw=>

It's The Pixel


Yesterday's DoubleClick marketing event appeared to be a success if a "few thousand viewers" via a livestream is any indication. The event announced new integrations within the DoubleClick marketing stack known formally as DoubleClick Digital Marketing. Invite Media-like tech is getting sucked into the DoubleClick For Advertiser ad server as exchange buying gets more efficient for the big DFA clients. There's more in AdExchanger's piece by Zach Rodgers <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7HrnXbtgJj9pZtzOXlnS8QS9nlPh1hty51HhgAWt3ES6vVZOthJSNht9nHYBVi1Nltbkf9jD1d2vnp_YB9yd8JQEGwG9M6sSueoBu4O6SZlAgatOOzynYhedPHmcD0KHSCg02eJeCRGdpY9BpAHy3CAxLpKo1ie7zKTJySU71FNSEUIyF-gtsOQbh7AuHf3xkAxqgjtHCmlKVo3F0qT-PMRqJnnKfC1Wv8eofFnChhzUYlRUlU7XhH2eGKhYlj9fN4=> . Here's the main thing - that pixel or cookie that you audience buyers love to use is now becoming available across channels ("Dart for Advertisers, Invite Media, DoubleClick Search, creative platforms (DoubleClick Studio, DoubleClick Rich Media and Teracent)"). It's synced - that's the idea anyway. For example, if you are buying search through DoubleClick Search, it will be even easier to retarget those fish that got away through display and the DoubleClick Ad Exchange because you can use the same cookie pool. Even Google competitor and Mediaocean CEO Bill Wise remarked to AdExchanger, "In a digital ad tech world where innovation has come in the form of hundreds of fragmented point solutions, this strategy is genius." Has Wise softened? Oh no, he's positioning as the independent alternative. Read even more about the event from Rebecca Lieb on iMedia Connection. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7E5yx_HHDN0Ct7t_zbVUXhp8lSSEdVTK1qFZyzZWmrXQx5Rd9uK428ItheGqKWAIXxua4PIddNpNOo1Q0Mv4zhZpzug94DkNUuSzg6YbrKGKW8FI0Hoph34HRP7LYCoJQhKblEXuIQIMA==>  


Oracle Adds To Social Intellect


Oracle is continuing to gobble up social media-related marketing companies. Yesterday's "victim" is a social listening service called Collective Intellect. The release explains, "Collective Intellect's cloud-based social intelligence solutions enable organizations to monitor, understand and respond to consumers' conversations on social media platforms such as Facebook and Twitter." If you know what the customer is saying, hopefully, you can better service them. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7FOSAd5-HpD5BMjSvNHwxBVrL6jANsocPXx9O2_F6yx9aAdqwGJCU2kG_srak9BsRgAWcYDVhM4TWkDOoEG0sdQJoOdm63qwFOUiNZVDB2MFkQNkqF7pg7SM-qkgSV1mHkvl1EyjPv_R589eIcBTlEFd6kc5IR-wA9MhnkFZ6iAszh9ChoJR0Bt0EQB37KL934forNMhiaAZQ==>  


2B Free Ads For Industry Push


The IAB has locked down more than two billion impressions for its "YourChoices" pro bono effort to spread the gospel, er, educate consumers about ad targeting. "This new industry campaign explains the benefits of online marketing communications, offers solutions for legitimate privacy concerns, directs consumers toward additional resources, and effectively demystifies the web," says a release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7FvTB_75zsfYlFgOpgEDkYJPBe7ZVxnFyAdhnRBOM6qrPxrdkWlCJAnZuvofgmXzCzvgiPKk7gxDATmoVt5FtaFgsNrTUT3hhYONMpt-v6xu5OjnrlDrt-YbkytqTB5Wj-O3AFhIerEALiGebFVfKqavm6T-veFB8xdRQTZwQuKBlqXoiidt4mfFMPfgCic6jCa6qYreM3Ed-Jbe6jilhDR> . Media space was donated by Google, Microsoft, Yahoo, and a couple dozen other ad nets and publishers. Its an extension of the "Privacy Matters" campaign, which launched three years ago with just 500 million donated ads. Seemed like a lot at the time. Quadruple the urgency? 


Facebook Targets Mobile


On ClickZ, Christopher Heine covers new mobile ad targeting available through Facebook as the social kingpin will allow advertisers to choose whether they want to target mobile or the PC via the company's sponsored stories product. TBG Digital CEO Simon Mansell tells ClickZ, "It 'opens up ads to businesses [that] have invested in building mobile apps,' (...). He said the development also creates opportunities for specifically targeting on-the-go consumers with products like suntan lotion and restaurant chain coupons." Or even insect repellant! Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7EQZvk3eUVJAV5kIGz_JCYZCQinUJbLld0lg6kJ055_gFhwAfkN0Lre03VY1HtUSEhQxp32YrP3HfvUJyq4sLg4LPqbZLwNXU_ShptDG8SFl5xZ0U6GgDyoNJTfZu-5sCeTihBITV9A-EKNkEa1G_aMOekyiWGdRxitL7wLRKahOQ7-iSz8B0rwQ5Olw5p2-JM=>  


More Place Data Please


To go big, hyperlocal needs to scale its data. PlaceIQ and Verve Wireless are hooking up to plug the former's place-based data - think photos, events, social actions - into Verve's ad platform. Says Verve CEO Tom MacIsaac, "We understand where the user is and PlaceIQ understands the context of that location and together we can help brand advertisers reach people based user segments that were otherwise unavailable in mobile." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7HcPy2a2p0WGMFGlR5L4MO-saf8jxCH2vBvhqETCSjftTYYk-wAgdkub3cRI-NvVTf63IyZogw_ThMj2jbUKrv-yIyny42aogHTVBCREPGziDWvDhYvkozTVxtf9AUirMZR1qRnaRnUNFArxtovhGqarzuISfrMrMQMqw0Hs3FA2qWXKaOCIsT4rJ49qYGAShDg-HYf6iaFNt6lNOD372yQ1wD7Cr6eWrHiT28WCdQLTA==>

Invite Media Founders Leave, Begin


"When Google called in early 2010 to 'explore the DSP space,' we were nervous. We wanted to be the one picked for the dance. We used to say that 'if Google was going to buy someone, we wanted it to be us,' and we meant it." And so goes the farewell-to-Google post on Nat Turner's personal blog as he and Invite Media co-founder Zach Weinberg are leaving Google to start a yet-to-be-fully-revealed "healthcare IT" company. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7Eh3vBZaNYHvA4wpKkMqRsEvkyEQzcP4-WgUzuRLrlOUGuCChV0XusCdUOKsK-m6J6sbUHQKTJxk4KDcOy8Ht15uxxXdtcPvXh2K9YtqxCcMkmp_1WuRSmYj5bJvf5v4e4=>  


The Chart


On GigaOm, Ki Mae Heussner reviews the history of the LUMA Partners chart with Terence Kawaja. Heussner teases,"So how did Kawaja know that he might be onto something with the slide? In part because of how the investment bankers around him were reacting. 'I'm of the view that, as you go through life, think about what an investment banker would do and do the opposite.'" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7FePTJXqjbbDE8UUWhgeh2RaRvoRT9Et18bo0TU7etDo2ZCmBVK50-UOiUqmdu4OZYoqP1hTjlZjTLNbpKoEviLxhr4kTSHpqRr3X6SGKB9Iux3sKhvdjHkmqLu3AomPaWoY6KFZUEUnWxORiY85BkZGMiiYIdprbbJBO9zfTDE8OXcvVAOh-JuxkemJeZbdBNOdgoW1Udv0yMplW0Y5x30>  Kawaja did his best Ricky Gervais at yesterday's DoubleClick marketing event, too. 


Check Printer Loves Marketing


Deluxe - you know, the check company - has bought internet marketing services company Orange Soda for $27.7 million. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7G2BMEh_RlRIiKiHKtZEwcJ0Gr226ad0qubnkAkf6lSoeXlJmBBrTna2J_cKPepRa7VCaznENeaievM1wjWqoP47BrY5m7FKWiFZUr9sPlMoEOWisUlUMW_n_FQHiQ6uAvigvNBra18N_gShTroBAgSSf32mjbw22x-VPcDZbq1K5a_RgZNiaK0tZk4zlJtNsU=> . How is this possible? Checks? Marketing? Well, Deluxe already has a marketing services unit and if you're familiar with the model used by American Express to target small business with an array of offerings (like Clickable and Adready), Deluxe is doing the same sort of thing. If you've got your hooks in a business, might as well offer them some help on the marketing front.


Brand Research


Solve Media has put a twist on its CAPTCHA ads and is now asking questions that speak to brand research with a tool called Brand Tags. Ad Age's Jason Del Rey explains, "Starting today, more and more of Solve's 4,500 partnering publisher sites will display Captchas that display a brand's logo instead of squiggly letters, and instruct web visitors to type in a word or phrase that they think best describes the brand." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VzByZwYGX7FoKxOT_m5p1jxqsEUjRg2vqOlotYTjzlVPOFR08W_yTtNRm35hcq8n90d4ypLYYSih3bZCCDNDiMHSwCIDzg2KBGwwEOdkaIYRA1wYpXN5bpyT6FFevcW_MkDSRP0fS4rSOQh5MMw6X-FFlIPhwH9G7RN8X2A0DBc1E2y-TN0hkYIDkBnbS1yXps-e3V6KypA7JCXnWU14jO6rhrDKN0fs>

Alt UDID Under Review


The Wall Street Journal sees the new UDID alternatives as mobile ad networks' efforts to "circumvent" Apple Safari browser security efforts. The WSJ says, "...Ad networks that serve advertisements within mobile apps have started using new identifiers that collect information like location and preferences as the user moves across apps. One of the tracking systems is based on a unique identifier located in the iPhone's wireless networking hardware-a system known as Open Device Identification Number, or ODIN." Privacy advocates claim the new data being captured could lead to PII without the user's consent. Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDgotazv4vijTDOuWQgFpYJNpz1Hjoqd1OR8XfEZie1Q-6_s1Ht4ZqdLL7govO8CnTCjFgVjBmIAp7JQOzIHr8jkd3iZ3sz-BU636Yt_NvDmZhikyh05WRPZ32l0tfhP3IofbwXm6fIImC6AlPl2KEv7K9bBrnM-QdUKfGYeeE00Vn_e0pQe40B8> 


Marketing's IT Project


Forbes Lisa Arthur eyes a prediction from Gartner analyst Laura McLellan that says "by 2017, CMOs will spend more on IT than their counterpart CIOs." Whoa, now. That's whole lotta IT. No wonder, though, as McLellan also predicts, "2012 IT budgets are expected to grow 4.7 percent, while all marketing budgets, in general, are predicted to grow 9 percent, and high tech marketing budgets, more specifically, are expected to increase 11 percent." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDgrUzb2QavHgBwir8W389g7mzg7lHeT20XZR0_yeqn1l-60wbQSGG0l_hkFzSQPybYpdG4tihBifmzBwaV87o-vDZFLnld6kKZiIToOFjYEBmxqDYsmLgtZOHaGI0vN9WSjr0MOSpsYChHoIlN5NJLzR74ZMygUGpD2Ju7UC2NK6tdNCHv0xQv0iLONE1c765Er4CW-awGC1id2rgv1q4KW-8ab5mHE66B3_2lqP-e9Og==> 


Segmenting Loyalty


The decision of New Orleans' daily paper The Times-Picayune to reduce its print production to only three days a week earlier this month has provoked a new round of hand-wringing about the life and death of the newspaper business. The hope is that as readers lower their reliance on expensive to deliver and distribute print, they'll naturally migrate to the paper's website to get their news fix. But the  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDieeXrDFB0vdow7D0RameM_vviL004SRhW7a7NxwXrpnx0jrJBgLwRmlITyjGweDzwhGTQ1banB_OzaRuRumwcmNtiRGmgTiEUusJBcZ5_HCWKfEgbNUF4ARU4SCzMuTIPqwfvpnFv-JXre4pdqeXguJKn1uxr8EgGJ4OF5drFRCXg4LFizHAH7YoNibwET2ODjbTY38scvcJ32kwoObIX_bt_Jp2yacsim7W4EGXqfEKaOMrPg7xlb> NYT's Christine Haughney quotes industry analysts who suggest readers' "sense of loyalty" would be lost along with the physical product. But the ultimate gamble is whether or not digital revenues will be able to pick up the slack more quickly. 


Parsing Real-Time Interests


On the Twitter Engineering blog, data visualization is the subject of a post titled, "Studying rapidly evolving user interests". How about tying your RTBing to real-time events and sentiment pulsing through Twitter? Twitter researcher Jimmy Lin doesn't go that far, but he does explain how his company approaches meausurement of the massive Twitter (or any 'big data') data sets, "One way to measure the dynamics of a content system is to test how quickly the distribution of terms and phrases appearing in it changes. A recent study we've done does exactly this: looking at terms and phrases in Tweets and in real-time search queries, we see that the most frequent terms in one hour or day tend to be very different from those in the next - significantly more so than in other content on the web. Informally, we call this phenomenon churn." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDjTUAPyCF-XMxA5pDLAAwX4a7awRy6OAGSxjoIrv0iCInND0b7zFYoA-qhyEuqp75E8c6_apfExSX2wFWZ9z2jlyWyIIr8qmnp5jH0arglFDr4ufoFh3vfoYBrwKMuRnZ1G-PMHhHlUaOA2uaeGDlzhJg79RGLZOq9oZQM7AnDnzk33g52ZZMTN> . And, download the paper on  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDjISRB2US39Q8MCzSzIF1mHWAjE6EEX9Z18jVrM92QFv45Ikj6Tqj1DehfD4hNC6f5-Zr7EpkU99zKyjvvI7HryLvPflejlS0K14brNU0QKXw6VMmej2IUX> "churn" (PDF).


NYC's Media Mayor
 

As New York City Mayor Mike Bloomberg looks toward the end of his third term and a return to running his company, New York Magazine's Gabriel Sherman offers an interesting comparison <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDjN2tpJVqwoXPGGAtboEeMCi70ZAk6i-fpHxF03niE879fcbyv6GZcbou43dpUDvp-dZeN4U5TFFw09JVSyoH1AlRAzzFRNXJ3QWYZ0uWdrlmIZwJCBdn_b-9I4UTM5IxoNgLaUKJI_RV_ywgZQWgBO>  of the media side of the business. "Bloomberg LP is like Google," he writes. "It has one wildly successful business model (selling data to banks in the case of Bloomberg; search in the case of Google). Efforts to expand beyond the core business of leasing terminals to financial firms have failed to produce similar results."

Analog Dollars to Facebook Dimes?


Facebook may have to wait, like, forever for ad spending to match the gobs of time its users spend with the site. Says this analysis by AdAge's Michael Learmonth,"The shift of dollars to attention will prove less linear and predictable for Facebook than for online display, which basically transplanted an approximation of the print ad model to the web -- or video, which is a transplant of TV's model." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDhgT0i6Tu5TMho1AdJyBk_nzjmUH-9c4q5bJsrXVuMTJiZ8d9lVDqLauZtt35HKI4DlNirEOrvll0RMlc03xwbP7BD94u-MUOD7hE0gU-sS1mU80NQ_A2ijEPRh4j_AEF4X6l76u33sn_FyQFRrftT8esIGzBdvYQTGHqK68ZEhxowXa6otDd9T91RD-ERgwqMNbJMijb7qig==> 


Boring Brand Dollars


Digital gangsta Ted Leonsis responds to a few questions from Tim Peterson on Adweek. About the shift of brand dollars online, Leonsis is sanguine, "We've certainly seen the search industry go from zero to $25-30 billion in a decade. That spending came from somewhere. We've certainly seen the online display business get to be $15-20 billion. That business came from someplace. But this video/television/long-form, that's waiting to be unlocked, and I think we'll see that with this commingling of video and social happening over the next four or five years." Read the whole interview <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDgThRPJKrdOydE72VExdJ2QMeiVa4kwOU8Id8464qMSxElm9dLFIBwp5VdCynDxJIkg6PGWbvWyik09TIVw8Hl7rDKrPSqtugxj7Gp_6paJnGDwLzOpGpZIk_83LOBukJ2cb_vF9aaVMttnqfVXRliXPqS1zCUxUt2Ulr3MsQjhQOcT2lY4QYE-> .


Bad Venture, Bad


On Mediapost, Namely's Matt Straz ponders a recent comment by the IAB's Randall Rothenberg, "Venture capital has supported and financed a bunch of chaos." As you might imagine, those in the venture capital world including Neu Ventures' Jerry Neumann think differently. Read about his retort. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDhhJZvyhVkTQHTvNqhobtfei5J2LJSLSwGQRgZzs1xFXNxAq7MK7YgHx5EDn3qip_FdXpOK4k2xG2UZ9YIKQ-LMhO0EhHqLt99H2BlHMCn0mk02uNRCWA3EzT5zGPSKAW4xFkk9KFdle9Rx2GEtwglxmX8GzepWTdLUtxJkhK8S-raQHhd_pGxgU_6HYTMsDDtfjbN7dndF84D4cTfKutRA8uR-jVsWGVM=>  Straz thinks aloud, "It is time for venture capitalists to commit to working more closely with the industry it aims to profit from and mitigate the chaos they are creating." Don't forget to read the comments on this one. 


Microsoft's TV Ad Network


Interactive TV advertising may be the wave of the future but right now, it's far from a big business. At least that's what Microsoft appears to have concluded, as the Redmond software giant is closing down its Microsoft Advertising TV Network, the unit charged with selling targeted TV ads based on set-top box data for cable networks run by Viacom and NBC Universal, reports  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDgKfBSYI1rl7B9sTkWAhQRQZPy2LZ0-5RMuVPzDr18z1-Eijx-58zPkm1zMZNaeQOplcnK9JEyaNvShJmUPLmtumvgQSJ5Y5o7vKTxsOdIYgiUcS2PhmIWu8Fryfrm6o3q58qEabyMCyNY5sdjaEqbS3WKPhAKJ_oU4TxVHyj84_x_OaaonQuTatImMIza3U3M=> Adweek's Mike Shields. As many as 15 staffers in the unit will also be laid off as Microsoft considers selling its Navic software business, which powers set-top box ads. The move comes a few months after the cable industry JV Canoe Ventures' abandoned efforts <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_9qVapKYZDiolLD4-dZoSlxP6OVLQBQYbOr_WAIY3TsgP2n01G74yEzP68pFwoWyuRP9LMl0XwnvV56k4zNt6-sGyPrYZYjDHkCsKfI1TbJESy1A8wEg87xY2xpWn7VK1J0F8dI6oZeUCcr7hOTnhGAMCKvGOEMNBoC5oyfAqx5yZTsi0o4Q4OAwwQiAQKFiPIgUDn5kRQQWbYZaD5CEUtVqMBEaVxcdhnB6zGUM-QxZ1k5nCSR_4Q==>  to forge a national targeted TV ad sales platform.

The Login Cometh


Michael Miller reports on Google execs Susan Wojcicki and Sundar Pichai's appearance at last week's D:10 conference. In response to a question about the poor targeting of advertising today, Miller paraphrases Pichai who says, "The personalization of advertising is still in its early days, with most ads placed based just on IP addresses and the sites they appear on. As more people are logged in and more people use mobile phones, advertising will get better, he said." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001AyNtajuJnZHrus-UdzgkLjUvZUZaAhTOnmOobFPWhMccivarsMSxgYuyV3fjEshZy-hsgiTWXYN17vnsUFXf1CdOOCaZCefgDxjnVBhkChjsGH--I6febMcG-5L0qWyVKDqPHnHhyPdHgNuhwJbjVXuH-zX2PBUUE0skM1P4gDKRm_lV9GBQViIwm8K7Af6P62BWFpWEw_g-snXE49T5IMv7PcYtXT0QZWtfxytx2AhJU7oLi0AckQ==> . The login is the key - it's the first party "cookie" with user's opt-in approval. Read the partial transcript on piracy, too, from the WSJ <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001AyNtajuJnZFdTjdw7RdBdO9WUnAOfHu1ahOZh7uuRAm2qhmf5ZmdIuV2VdsgHQV6Z2kALBOOMmg6sjQNiUee_5gMsLw6t0QiuxbO4sMl6hvskx4kqInQDOeB_Hjx7nA4IAJd-wLWYbnUXZShMFQzC2GKtuoThXSHk_RvcQKJPiMDXpq7sAnjDrjrhehAxLMQ> . And, read this one one on a new Google local ads initiative here (subscription <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001AyNtajuJnZGdt79Fv5N1VnYM4QBeBnvAEdqq35uBQ_xa6gGw9tuYOuiNhv57ycpXNFsEnFTE-4cY-xJ2VH5yQMSdFp_UL53nWlSJCArUC1q3I16P0TdJuOZUZj7YZmNk7qSpoYNazKiyTQT6ak6i4d9OHUIuQM17Pfxw9T7VvQH-zHChVCCl6dTrZXnVbbx5> ). In effect, it depends on the Google+ login.


Educating The Masses


Demand-side platform MediaMath sees an opportunity to educate potential clients and its fellow Direct Marketing Association members with its "New Marketing Institute" initiative. MediaPost's Joe Mandese explains, "The ad technology education initiative is (intended) to fill the educational void needed to keep digital media buyers up to snuff within an industry that is being transformed by rapid advancements in technology, especially computerized systems for targeting the best consumers, and so-called 'programmatic' methods for buying them." Recruiting In Israel


In a video interview with Technion, Israel Institue of Technology, Akamai co-Founder and Chief Scientist Tom Leighton discusses his company and its content distribution network business. What's clear in the interview is that Akamai is moving at least some of its recruiting efforts to Israel as competition for qualified engineers heats up. In reference to Akamai's recent purchase of Israel-based Contendo, Leighton says (at around 15:00), "This probably won't be the last acquisition we do in Israel." See it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001AyNtajuJnZGtzYS7aAGUc0LNSVaT3NARfuk09ZLL3rq-i5XMX6WgYzfI91HAgvTCtA2KSKSAUVfH3iCZ_132E33eunD_sm7ODoYZZHTAYU085oKgaKsHMDGUgdniFhLbZsfUJUm8WMpd9aJRbhRWkw==> . I will confess that my own employer, Forrester Research, has been a bit dishonest on this topic, with my assistance." And then after a few stats, he adds, "Unlike other computing form factors - the desktop, the laptop - the tablet will have no permanence whatsoever." So what will? DNT Set To "ON"


If you just can't stand browsing without a Do-Not-Track feature, in a few days Microsoft says it can help with DNT Features built into its latest Internet Explorer 10. Read the news buried in a news release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZVe7CQj5GmAV5stM_3zLiXemAtFbxpvzdkkezP5BX2LHFx0plxfu10T2cGQPJUiMHKmJ8wWBhn2sqUDK0GwlYHQDTdvnT10gVfJOObFsdWNCJAe2H3og2a8Rwc2yqNpEQav5Xxk0863wdBoyPmodR5l92yQcXZtRXVuc4xZlVQvjfUYRfrXxL6g> . Meanwhile, IAB CEO Randall Rothenberg isn't happy as he says the DNT feature is set to "ON" by default in the Windows version. He tells IAB members, "This represents a step backwards in consumer choice, and we fear it will harm many of the businesses, particularly publishers, that fuel so much of the rich content on the internet." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZV7k1ub2hVPfcyJhIdzWSzO-KPhAG5ajcemv1ubqnhDSZBvzo6SlSIupA2w8bX19e5hUnsP43i1ZioeR0Z_LkL2VrR-mGLfmbJ055Qij7a021ZE9BsOYE-K> . On that note, the DAA is "concerned," too. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZUz_vAo1iV02V5115pqVyla1Bd8Ub-mq5g1KaJPsk_krKk24LLJ2ccyw_XmxtMt-rec_ko5eCga_CxiVhIQ_kSs9Uh3VaEUhpwINbGN56F2zeWvamr3oKf-QcY2Jo_cpzhyx-0O64X8yxn9be_DkJ1DNH8CqLOn7ErjuopvKvOo2aYNnomTqolbmN76VwcxQWQ84PtLktjXBirmhSuyCMzB1Pchtuz8-66pFDkWoJMdXg==> 

A Microsoft spokesperson responds, "Multi-stakeholder discussions regarding the appropriate response to the DNT signal are ongoing and we look forward to continuing to participate in them. We believe a consistent industry-wide response is important in order to provide a consistent consumer experience across the web. As we announced in February <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZUARragE-Vek2A6e9k-szwou-mLzWsZDN4k8AaVDnRyb9SAs_sBuUh3dGTJKFmUGSCYFy_MdHqV9P0s_dosf3Npdg1CKUNooyqk5QXtXQxmQliC1kaW9KfiEU9gVZVatOxWhW2rOMVS2Sxf95EPUbIANUvgR-UsX7NApmh7eLDEmho-lYUVWyIr1q1lXBG3jmurhXVWX6Iptz191jk34EQKwnp0AqC_fJSyrPRV4wqmAB-Z0UPbCs5LlWHdVnbL204=> , Microsoft Advertising intends to treat the do-not-track browser signal as an opt-out of behavioral advertising under the Digital Advertising Alliances self-regulatory program. Microsoft does not yet respond to the DNT signal, but we are actively working with other advertising industry leaders on what an implementation plan for DNT might look like, with a goal of announcing more details about our plans in the coming months."


Invite Media Integration?


A "big event" is planned on Monday by Google's DoubleClick unit as display insiders anticipate the next rev on the platform. No word on what the news is exactly but Invite Media's integration into DoubleClick For Advertiser ad server - DFA 2.0 - may be at hand as exchange buying (and other stuff) is integrated in the advertiser-side ad server. Or, how about the somewhat stealthy DoubleClick Data Plaform (DDP!) - is Google on the verge of launching a data management platform layer that provides easy access for exchange buyers to third-party data sets? Or how about an Admeld integration update? Or? Or? Read a bit more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZVXD4oIfZnuMm1iPC0hsduaO6Ihm8GWbq0E_JyXwZSwIf4BB7wCmMGt8ZMBE5ocPMOYZxlF8CW1qfqAzIl-2gDz2yEwXPOL1JtSLohxXyGBeJzkmFfMAs_gg--Me8E4HrOlpSYhvZ3cxd46oFho8k06> . A live stream will be available. 


Mobile Web Vs App


Digiday's Josh Sternberg explores the debate publishers are having on whether to go Mobile Web or App with their publications. Responses vary - even within a response - as Nat Geo president Declan Moore says, "Both. At National Geographic, we're happy with the scale we are achieving with our native app interactive edition for the magazine, using Adobe DPS to integrate with existing print workflows and provide added texture to our storytelling narrative, including the addition of popular video elements." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZXqegCTvS1Pd2w3m-4ziV86z2wrovcY-GmYnyDik_jIM8fwQxmjNlz0JR-_imRqp95NQMuku_Z5q6N-qOxQCLlwanc1nKxywHc1w0fjWcygYhDzIFuW15f9gsUzt2-heSBbvyylgJnyrltIeBW3jiau>  


Was Product Search, Now Shopping


On The Google Commerce blog, Sameer Samat, vp of product, Google Shopping, announces that the company is dumping its free product search listings known as Google Product Search in exchange for paid ones called Google Shopping. The reasoning is... better data: "Higher quality data-whether it's accurate prices, the latest offers or product availability-should mean better shopping results for users, which in turn should create higher quality traffic for merchants." And, more Google revenue. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZUEOuq72QExyT3HIrYYfgBQ38ty8dZ6EQ-f6drBggzHqFVI23VUlxwUpkrWm6M8Z6Y6dMsCauo9PPD5JeNRaPS3Qi16LXg3lI6KBrGczpeRLOKcC9mvLA2jBJ8RqnwgUNF53h86P1XhFWXfEa1xEnJQxCW1nKBmCwNcVfDBEx-X9TBhEonJK6NXDGfuN4UQsco=>  Imagine if Google made its "regular" search engine with paid listings? - a la GoTo from days of yore <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZVbZIt6E9YFDE0-PXkc--gQj9IZDGUBU2bCgLfccEjMOC1OU6CccRIsLPppwv1UhmKRO1z19Gh9U5MIHkkKiXzN3QT9evPH630pUA9DAR98kcIUWmhrQFoOCC9IGkKHdYuIyrO-ntrcsRUksxJ2qCWz> . Search Engine Land's Danny Sullivan sees a strategic shift by Google as it accepts paid inclusion into its product search engine. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZWuN9FBKRU09b6sJIGMjIsHBif-N30Kg0JvJIe1anoydyUee0zJQ5dqj-0YIIHsnmaPhU-V49BHc3_D8IomHheWPM0LlLyXisxj1ZqEnDoSaxeZ1LkMhKwOUz-hyl0px2VBdNnzOJY3KvwnBSDdCCaj2hAJISYChtf8Pu9wQ1qbhXbnRM9qZ7lFEURljh5xZwpTKHev3AuWn6H3oJiaMaeA> . 


Rich Media Rules


On ClickZ, Tessa Wegert offers 10 Do's and Don'ts for rich media advertising. Cross-channel integration is a biggy for the "Do's" column: "Make your online rich media ads consistent with your offline ads, social media presence, and product site. There is much to be said for creating an integrated cross-media experience, particularly when it comes to encouraging product and message recall." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001bZkWD4GTFZU8Q4yPYqoghq52K4x--1evo1ikEFIE1aSRGLhSrf6hezR9NUoBrbWv4pxuUyBCp9NtaVmor8CCFgyZwVCNnR-xd1FKJtAjhvnFWVSvET66iQzz5Uljh6bN8qFEU1hVcLiHW9265gphdBIImpaV31cCnN5WD31GCHBX9QL7F5gWWQ==>
